The Hunting Law Promulgated by the National Government 86

The text of the Hunting Law promulgated by the National Government on the 28th is as follows: (Article 1) Hunting as referred to in this law refers to the capture of birds and animals with hunting tools or hawks and dogs. (Article 2) The types and names of hunting tools and restrictions shall be determined by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Industry in accordance with local conditions. (Article 3) The birds and animals referred to in this law are divided into the following four categories: 1. Birds and animals that harm humans; 2. Birds and animals that are harmful to livestock, crops, forests, and trees; 3. Birds and animals that are beneficial to crops, forests, and trees; 4. Other birds and animals that can be used as food or supplies. The names of the birds in each of the preceding categories shall be determined by the Ministry of Industry. (Article 4) The birds and animals in the first category of the preceding article may be hunted at any time. The birds and animals in the third category may not be hunted except for those who are specially permitted for academic research. The opening and closing dates for hunting the birds and animals in the second and fourth categories shall be determined separately by the municipal and county governments each year. (Article 5) Hunters shall apply to the municipal and county governments of the hunting area for approval and registration and obtain a hunting permit, except for hunting the birds and animals in the first category of Article 3. However, those who do not have the nationality of the Republic of China shall be specially permitted by the National Government. (Article 6) In addition to the hunting law, the hunting permit shall contain the following information: 1. The hunter's name, age, nationality, occupation, and domicile or residence; 2. The types and names of the birds and animals to be captured; 3. The name of the hunting tool; 4. The hunting area; 5. The validity period; 6. The permit number. The hunting permit fee is one national currency dollar. (Article 7) Hunters who do not carry a hunting permit shall not hunt. (Article 8) Hunters shall not enter other people's gardens, cultivated land, or enclosed land without the consent of the occupant or caretaker. (Article 9) Hunting shall not be done using automobiles, steamships, or aircraft. (Article 10) Hunters shall not hunt at night without special permission. (Article 11) The following persons shall not hunt: 1. Minors; 2. The insane; 3. Soldiers or police officers; 4. Those who have been punished under this law and have not passed one year. (Article 12) Hunting is not allowed in the following places: 1. Historical sites and scenic spots; 2. Parks; 3. Roads and public waterways; 4. Places where people live or where crowds gather; 5. Unharvested cultivated land; 6. Other places designated by the Ministry of Industry, provincial, municipal, and county governments, or local police agencies, or places where hunting is prohibited with the approval of the people. (Article 13) Hunting shall not be done by the following methods: 1. Explosives; 2. Poisons; 3. Strong drugs; 4. Pitfalls. In special circumstances where the preceding methods must be used, an application shall be submitted to the municipal and county governments and police agencies for approval, and the hunting area shall be announced and posted in advance. (Article 14) The hunting season shall be from November 1 of each year to the end of February of the following year. If there are special circumstances during the preceding period, the municipal and county governments may advance or postpone the period and may extend it. In addition to the announcement, the matter shall be reported to the higher-level official agency for collection and transfer to the Ministry of Industry for record. In areas with a large number of birds and animals, the municipal and county governments shall stipulate the opening and closing dates for hunting each type of bird or animal. (Article 15) The municipal and county governments shall announce the types and names of birds and animals for which hunting is prohibited each year before the opening of the hunting season. (Article 16) The municipal and county governments and police agencies may suspend hunting in any of the following circumstances: 1. When martial law is declared; 2. When bandits are discovered; 3. When the birds and animals allowed to be hunted need protection; 4. When the places allowed to be hunted need to be prohibited from hunting. (Article 17) Those who violate Articles 4, 6, 8, 11, 12, and 13 shall be fined up to 50 yuan and may have their hunting permits revoked. (Article 18) The rules for the implementation of this law shall be determined by the Ministry of Industry. (Article 19) The date of implementation of this law shall be determined by order.

The Recovery of Anyuan County, Jiangxi Province 87

The Pseudo 20th Army Almost Completely Annihilated - The Provincial Government Commended the Former Magistrate of Xunwu

A dispatch from Nanchang reports that a porter who escaped from the bandit area of Nanfeng said, "Zhu, Mao, and Peng held a pseudo-people's conference on the border of Shaowu last month and spoke to the crowd, saying that in the future, the Red Army will follow the 'Four No-Fight Principles', that is, they will not fight when the National Army is powerful, they will not fight when the fortifications are strong, they will not fight when the sacrifices are too great, and they will not fight when the place is too poor. The pseudo-135 Army Corps consists of no more than ten thousand people, many of whom are children aged twelve or thirteen. They have dirty heads and faces, wear single clothes and barefoot, and have breakfast but no lunch. They eat today but do not know what they will eat tomorrow." From this, we can see the true nature of the Red Bandits. Zhu, Mao, Peng, and other bandits all failed in their recent westward attacks on Fuzhou and Jianchang, eastward attacks on Guangze and Shaowu, and northward peeks into western Zhejiang. The bandit nests on the border of southeastern Jiangxi and northwestern Fujian have been completely exhausted of grass roots and tree bark since the Nationalist Army of the four provinces of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, and Zhejiang jointly blockaded them. The pseudo-village Soviets of Ruijin and Changting urgently urged the payment of land taxes. Residents were either dead or fled. The bandit army had no way to plunder. Like hungry rats emerging from their holes, Chen Yi's unit of the pseudo-20th Army in southern Jiangxi was sent to Anliao to loot Longnan, Qiannan, and Dingnan.

After receiving the report, Yu Hanmou, the commander of the First Army of Guangdong in southern Jiangxi, made strict arrangements in advance. The Wang Zanbin Division of the Gui Army served as the middle route and was assigned to attack the front of Anyuan. The Ye Zhao Department of the Second Division of the Guangdong Army flanked the left side of the bandits from Xinfeng. The Chen Zhang Department of the Independent Second Brigade encircled the right side of the bandits. On the 19th of this month, they advanced to the vicinity of Anyuan. They engaged in fierce battles with the bandits outside the city. The Nationalist Army advanced bravely and fiercely, killing many bandits. The bandits retreated in a panic to the east. At that time, Xie Zheng's regiment of the Third Army in Xunwu and Li Hanhun's unit of the Independent Third Division received Yu Hanmou's telegram ordering them to block the area. When the bandits fled to Bentiao, dozens of miles west of Xunwu County, they were cut off by Xie Zheng's regiment. The bandits were trapped in the core area. Just as they were breaking through the encirclement and fighting fiercely, Li Hanhun's division also arrived and joined the coordination. The bandit army was fragmented and scattered, unable to escape. Those who could not escape surrendered their weapons. As a result, Anyuan was recovered by Guangdong and Guangxi on the 20th. After Yu Hanmou received the telegram reporting the recovery of Ancheng, he considered that the county was located in a remote area on the border of Guangdong, had been occupied by bandits for a long time, the people's livelihood was exhausted, and the area was devastated. It was essential to have someone responsible for rescuing the dead and healing the wounded. He specially appointed Lai Jianhou, a counselor of the First Army Headquarters, as the magistrate of Anyuan County to handle the aftermath. In addition to telegraphing the headquarters of the three provinces' suppression of bandits on the 21st to report the victory, Yu also telegraphed the provincial government to appoint Lai as the magistrate of the county to take full responsibility, and allocated funds to provide urgent relief.

The former Magistrate of Xunwu County, Pan Mengchun, died in battle against the bandits in the county in March. His son, Pan Zuoyun, was also captured and killed because he was a staff member of the county government. The provincial government specially provided condolences and funeral expenses of 2,000 yuan, in accordance with the cases of Ji Gongquan, the Magistrate of Anfu County, and Wu Zhaofeng, the Magistrate of Xinfeng County, who died in the maintenance of the border, to comfort the loyal souls. (December 23)

Ma Hongkui Passes Through Jinan to Peiping 88

Going to Ningxia to Assume the Position of Chairman, Mr. Ma's Talk When Passing Through Jinan

A dispatch from Jinan states that Ma Hongkui, Chairman of the Ningxia Provincial Government and Commander-in-Chief of the 15th Route Army, arrived in Jinan by car from Nanjing, intending to go to Ningxia to take office. The car arrived in Jinan at 7:30 PM today (the 27th). The provincial government secretary-general Zhang Shaotang, finance minister Tu Xiangce, headquarters chief of staff Liu Shuxiang, staff section chief Zhang Guoxuan, provincial capital public security bureau Wang Kairu, and pistol brigade commander Lei Taiping all arrived at the station to welcome him. Ma got out of the car and shook hands with the greeters one by one, then made a statement to the press, saying that he had left Beijing last night and planned to meet with Chairman Han after arriving in Beiping. He would stay in Ping for a few days and would not return to Xinyang. After half of the troops had been sent to Ningxia, he would go to Ningxia to take office. The troops he was taking were the Lu Zhongliang, Ma Baolin, and Ma Yingcai brigades. The cavalry brigade remained in Henan, with brigade commander Ma Xiaojiao temporarily acting as commander-in-chief, waiting for his elder brother (Ma Hongbin) to arrive and take over. The troops would begin to move tomorrow and the day after. They would get off the train in Baotou and walk, and it would take another two weeks to arrive. He had left Ningxia in the winter of the 15th year of the Republic and had been away for several years. This time in Beijing, he had expressed to Chairman Chiang that he would maintain the current situation in the short term. When the central government had concrete plans for the northwest in the future, he planned to go abroad to see. Regarding Ningxia, the 7th Division was currently stationed there. Opium prohibition in Gansu was very difficult. Planting was too widespread. If the people did not grow opium, they would have nothing to live on. If the people were not allowed to grow it, other troops would also grow it, which was impossible. A few days ago, his troops laid off four or five thousand people. In addition to the old and weak, the disabled and those injured in suppressing bandits accounted for 2,000 people. Most of his troops were from Gansu, with Gansu people accounting for 80-90% of the officers and 30% of the soldiers. When he was a company commander, the troops he led were not only from one county, but also from one township. When he went home, the fathers and elders invited him to their homes on the 50-mile road from the county seat to his hometown. Fathers asked him for their sons, and wives asked him for their husbands. There were cries everywhere along the way until he got home at night. If he went back this time, he thought there would be even more people asking for people. He was overwhelmed with emotion. At 8:30, Mr. Ma boarded the train and headed north. (December 27)

Fifth Day of the Jiangsu Provincial Representatives' Assembly 89

The Third Jiangsu Provincial Representatives' Assembly held its fifth general meeting today (the 29th) at 10:00 AM. One hundred and six representatives from various counties attended. After Chairman Xu Yongji opened the meeting, he reported: (A) Regarding the report on the administrative work of various agencies, due to the central instructor Hong Ludong's departure for Beijing last night, there were no concrete measures yet. (It is heard that the provincial government, due to the excessive questioning of the Civil Affairs Director by the representatives the previous day, considered it exceeding the scope and expressed imprudent words, and had sent a letter to the presidium of the assembly yesterday, stating that it would be inconvenient to attend. Therefore, the heads of various provincial departments have suspended reporting on their work for the past two days. This matter is currently being mediated by the central instructor Hong Ludong). The agenda is now changed, and the report is postponed. (B) The date of visiting the mausoleum has not yet been decided and will be notified after the decision. After the report, the motions were discussed. (1) The motion to effectively improve the water conservancy of the Jiangbei Canal was resolved to be handed over to a special committee. (2) The motion to request that the name of the district party headquarters be uniformly called the county party headquarters was resolved to be handed over to the next executive committee for handling. (3) The motion to effectively promote district autonomy and complete the political tutelage work in this province was resolved to be passed as it stands, and the next executive committee will send a letter to the provincial government to effectively implement it. (4) The motion to request the central government to complete the Huai River diversion project as soon as possible to maintain the people's livelihood was resolved to be passed. (5) The motion to set a deadline for the completion of county roads in various counties was resolved to be passed.

The sixth general meeting was held at 2:30 PM, with 124 representatives present, and Chairman Sheng Xiru continued to discuss the motions. (1) The motion to request the construction of a connecting line between the Beijing-Hangzhou and Beijing-Jian railway lines to facilitate transportation was resolved to be passed. (2) The petition to the central government to quickly determine and implement land value tax measures to alleviate the suffering of the people of Jiangsu and facilitate progress was resolved to be passed. (3) The motion to abolish the rural public security organs and strengthen the people's self-defense forces to ensure safety and benefit the people's livelihood was resolved to be passed. (4) The motion to telegraph Tang Yulin, the chairman of the Rehe provincial government, to resolutely resist Japan to consolidate national defense was resolved to be passed. (5) The motion to abolish the finance, public security, and construction bureaus of various counties and establish departments to handle affairs in order to save expenses was resolved to be passed. (6) The motion to universally establish county courts, implement the spirit of judicial independence, to prevent malpractices and protect civil rights was resolved to be passed according to the original method. At this point, the chairman announced a recess.

Opinion Paper on the Huai River Diversion Project by Engineering Experts from the League of Nations (Continued) 90

The undersigned have been shown many broken maps of the Huai River in the west, and have also been instructed on the methods for setting the height of embankment gradients and embankment distances at specified locations. From this, we know that everything has been carefully planned, allocating the necessary commercial area to prevent the largest flood volume in history.

However, in order to suit these conditions, the embankment distance should be extremely wide. Buying land is obviously not feasible given the current economic situation. Therefore, in the first phase, the Huai River Diversion Committee had to reluctantly implement a less-than-ideal plan, limiting its work to repairing existing embankments and constructing new embankments near the Huai River, with a distance of only half a kilometer to one kilometer, and a top height slightly lower than the one that should be built.

The Huai River embankment construction plan currently being implemented, approximately 400 kilometers downstream of the Honghekou, does not include the length of the embankments of various tributaries. Judging from the list, approximately 50 percent of the extraordinary flood volume of 1921 or 1931 (year 10 and year 20 of the Republic of China) can be contained between the embankments.

Within this limited flood discharge range, the undersigned, after examining the completion of this portion of the plan, can prove its perfection and effectiveness. To prevent the vast area of arable land that has been flooded in the past from being affected by floods, it can be seen that repairing the Huai River embankment and handling the flood discharge on Hongze Lake are urgent tasks. After all the above-mentioned projects are carried out, the frequent floods and droughts of the past can be avoided.

As for the Shanghai tributaries of the Huai River, and the proposed corrections and inclusions in several places, the undersigned suggest that before any engineering is implemented, the possible effects on the Huai River's flow and the rate of runoff and water scenery from the affiliated water receiving areas should be carefully considered.

The committee members further suggest that the proposed direct engineering through Gaozhuang near Shuanggou on Hongze Lake to shorten the Huai flow should not be carried out until after precise measurements of the water surface height at both ends of the proposed excavation during floods. Establishing the height of the two exhaustion surfaces proves that there is insufficient benefit to justify the use of engineering as we have deduced. Furthermore, this matter may be found to be rocky or interspersed with extremely difficult-to-excavate soil during the preliminary work necessary, making it difficult to implement.

After discussing the upper reaches of the Huai River, the undersigned now mention that the river at the current Bengbu railway bridge must be expanded.

As for the Hongze Lake Huai River Diversion Committee's plan to build embankments around the lake to increase the existing capacity of this natural reservoir, so that during short flood periods, a portion that cannot be safely discharged can be retained in the middle, the plan is to maintain the lake level at 13.60 meters above the Yellow River zero point after each major flood discharge. According to this calculation, the volume between the above-mentioned water level and 12.50 meters, or 11.00 meters, the lowest drop in the upstream drought, is sufficient for irrigation until the next spring and summer flood. At any time, the lake water must be lowered to 12.50 meters before the next upstream flood, if necessary, using the proposed movable dam at Jiangba to control it.

During the flood season, the amount of lake water discharged should be adjusted to suit the discharge capacity of the downstream. The excess water is stored in the lake, as mentioned above. During extraordinary floods, the maximum flood volume is determined to be 15,000 cubic meters per second. The Huai River Diversion Committee plans to discharge 5,000 to 6,000 cubic meters of lake water per second during this period, depending on the water level of the Yangtze River at the time. According to this, the water level in the lake will gradually increase, the former reaching a maximum of 15.65 meters, and the latter reaching 16.10 meters. The Hongze Lake surrounding embankment is built to 1.50 meters above the flood level.

The undersigned express their approval of the plan, and feel that it not only solves the Huai River flood control problem, but also the shipping and irrigation problems. The land within the lake embankment below 13.60 meters will inevitably be submerged and cannot be cultivated. However, everyone knows that this is all unowned land. In any case, the benefits of shipping and irrigation downstream of Hongze are related to the country and are more important.

Currently, the Huai River flood water discharged from Hongze Lake is unadjusted, and its main outlet passes through the Sanhe and Gaobao-Xian-Shaobo lakes. There is also the Zhangma River that flows from Hongze Lake into the canal, and the Liuzha and Shaobo Lake water merge. Then, each stream flows through the five diversion canals and into the Yangtze River. In years of high water, due to the obstructed tail, the water cannot be discharged to its full extent, and the banks of the canal east and west break, and the vast fields are submerged. Some water remains all year round, causing great disasters. If the Yangtze River can conveniently accept the flood volume, it has not been proven that it cannot temporarily accommodate more water. Therefore, the Huai River Diversion Committee plans to control the amount of lake water discharged to suit the downstream situation, while still maintaining the original Sanjiangying inlet as the main flood discharge channel, and using direct access to the sea as a supplement.

Before commenting on the Huai River Diversion Committee's plan, the undersigned can now state that after on-site inspections and careful research on the proposed indirect or direct access to the sea waterways, we have not seen any economical or complete method that can be used to achieve the main purpose of the diversion. Therefore, except for the future possibility of using the access to the sea waterway to discharge a small portion of the flood water as a way to increase safety, the undersigned feel that this plan does not need further research.

In order to regulate the discharge of lake water, it is proposed to build a movable dam near Jiangba to control the flow of lake water through the Sanhe and Gaobao lakes, and below the newly built ship lock in Shaobo. If so, the Huai River flood water between Hongze Lake and Shaobo will be controlled within a single established waterway. The west embankment of the canal will no longer be as dangerous as it has been, and it can be seen that the existing ports on the west embankment do not need to be protected and should be permanently blocked during construction. Although the undersigned all agree with the plan, we believe that there is no special increase in the amount of flood discharge achieved by building double embankments in Gaobao Lake to form a river channel. Therefore, we recommend that this part of the plan be given more precise study before implementing this extremely costly project.

As for the movable dam to be built in Jiangba to discharge the maximum amount of 9,000 cubic meters per second, it is estimated that a total width of 600 meters of sluice gates must be installed. The appropriate style and method of operation of the sluice gates must be determined based on the results of a complete examination of the dam site. Regarding this point, as well as the addresses of other proposed dams mentioned above, the undersigned feel that it is necessary to carry out thorough and precise drilling to determine the nature of the underlying geological layers before proceeding with the construction of the planned dam project. The undersigned have been informed of the drilling methods that have been used there, but feel that the results obtained or the degree of accuracy are still open to discussion. For such an important project to be undertaken, the undersigned consider it necessary to first use a four-inch soil drill to penetrate the ground and then recover a layer of oil to extract the central tube for examination, and record the depth.

Within the Zhangma River discharge channel of Hongze Lake, the Huai River Diversion Committee is planning to build a ship lock near Huaiyin to regulate flood discharge, realign the canal, rebuild the Zhiji Dam as a discharge gate, and build several diversion canals. The undersigned believe that the plan will achieve its intended purpose, but we recommend that if the proposed ship lock is moved southwest about two miles, so that it is located in a place where only a shorter new river channel is needed, the cost will be greatly saved.

In addition, the flood control problem related to the eastern part of the Shandong Canal requires the waters of the Si River, Yi River, and Shu River, the current state of which is deeply related to the flood situation of the Canal and its surroundings. The Huai River Diversion Committee plans to dredge the above-mentioned rivers separately, so that each has a tail outlet to discharge flood water, while allocating and supplying water to the central canal for shipping and irrigation needs. The undersigned feel that this is very appropriate.

In the preceding sections, the undersigned have reluctantly described the important issues arising from the improvement of the current state of the Huai River. Flood control is the main goal and has been satisfactorily resolved, while the convenience of Huai shipping, irrigation, and increased traffic is easy to achieve. Therefore, the undersigned recommend that the following projects should be held first and should not be delayed: (1) the movable dam at Jiangba, (2) the ship lock at Shaobo and the necessary repairs to the west embankment of the Canal, (3) the ship lock near Huaiyin and the reconstruction of the Xiji Dam as a discharge gate, (4) the surrounding embankment of Hongze Lake.

In addition, special attention should be paid to diverting the Shandong Si River flood water into Hongze Lake to reduce the problems of the current state of the Canal, and it is proposed that the Liudong ship lock be completed as soon as possible. After the above-mentioned projects are completed and the embankments to be built in the upper reaches of the Huai River are continued, the flood control problem can be definitively resolved, and the drought situation today will be greatly improved, and the river bank on the six floodgates will be opened. Therefore, before concluding, the undersigned would like to briefly offer their opinion on the design of the shipping ship lock to be built in the Canal. We believe that it may be beneficial to review it. That is, in the preliminary design of the Huai River Diversion Committee, the entrance width of the ship lock is set at eleven meters. After investigating the dimensions of the largest ships currently navigating in the Canal, the width restrictions of the waterway, and the water depth obtained during the dry season after the increase in shipping convenience, the undersigned believe that this width is too large and can be reduced to eight or nine meters, which would greatly save costs. Regarding this issue, the undersigned can cite the Beicang ship lock project, which is currently being handled by the Hai River Improvement Committee in the Yongding River management plan and has recently been completed. The undersigned recommend that the responsible design and construction personnel of the ship lock to be built in the Canal go to examine the details of the case, which would be extremely useful. (End)

Eighty-One-Year-Old Woman Murdered in Suspected Robbery Case 91

Yang Su, a farmer in the Xiaoyouche area of the Second District, is 81 years old, owns over 100 mu of land, and has several thousand yuan in cash. She only has two daughters, both of whom are married. One daughter died after marriage. Because she had no male heir, she adopted a son with a different surname, Yang Mengsheng, but she did not get along with Mengsheng and treated him like a stranger. She was also unwilling to provide for her nephew Yang Guisheng and Yang Guilin, and planned to give all of her property to her daughters, which aroused resentment from Mengsheng, Guisheng, and Guilin. The day before yesterday afternoon, Mengsheng and others suddenly reported that their home had been robbed the previous night, and Yang Su had been murdered. The district office immediately forwarded the letter to the Zhubqiao Public Security Fifth Branch, and Branch Chief Kang Fasheng went to investigate. There were no signs of a break-in. Branch Chief Kang found many suspicious points in the case and reported it to the county government to send personnel to the countryside for examination. It was discovered that there was a rope mark around Yang Su's neck, and it seemed that she had been strangled to death with a rope, which was very suspicious. The county sent Zhao Cheng, an investigating officer, and Zheng Yue, along with four police officers, secretly to investigate by small Huinan Wheel last night, and ordered the police to summon Yang Mengsheng and others to wait for interrogation. However, Yang Mengsheng had already fled. Only his wife, Zhang, and the local clerk, Zhu Jinkang, were summoned. They were immediately taken to the county for interrogation.

A Tragic Accident Involving a Car in Qingjiang 102

A car from the Huaiyin Yangzhong Automobile Company was traveling from Gaoyou to Qingjiang on the 19th. When passing through the Xiaojinghe area of Huai'an County, the car overturned because the roadbed was on the Yunjihe embankment, the top of the embankment was narrow, and there was a telephone pole standing in the middle of the road, causing the driver to be careless. All eight male and female passengers were seriously injured, and one female passenger died due to serious injuries. The injured passengers have now gathered in Qingjiang to seriously negotiate with the company.

The situation has been reported everywhere." The above does not match your newspaper's report. In order to avoid misleading people, we specially request that you make a correction. Chairman Zhang Junguang of the National Salvation Association is Missing 109

Received Threatening Letters Several Days Ago

Searched Everywhere, But There is Still No Trace

Guowen News Agency reports that Zhang Junguang, the executive director of the National Salvation Associations of All Circles, has been actively involved in the anti-Japanese movement. He has previously received many threatening letters from the so-called Protection Corps and the Sino-Japanese Greater Harmony Association, which he dismissed with a smile. However, he suddenly disappeared the day before yesterday (the 28th). There is much suspicion that the clues are related to the previous letters. He is very filial to his parents and would never leave without saying goodbye. Here are the details of the situation:

Disappearance Details 110

On the 28th, at around 10 AM, Mr. Zhang bid farewell to his mother and left, mentioning he was going to the Bankers' Association for a special publication advertisement for the National Salvation Association, and to meet with Mr. Lin (Kanghou). He said if he couldn't return home for lunch, he would definitely notify them by phone. However, the family waited until 1:30 PM, but there was no phone call, causing great anxiety. Because Mr. Zhang was filial to his parents and always informed them before leaving and returned on time, he had never been overdue, causing his mother to wait anxiously. The previous day, they waited until dinner but he didn't return, so they sent people out in all directions to search for him. For two days now, there has been no trace of him. The two elderly Mr. and Mrs. Zhang have only this son, and they don't know if he is safe or in danger, causing them to faint several times.

A Brief Biography of Mr. Zhang 111

Mr. Zhang is from a prominent family in Nanhui, Jiangsu. He studied in Japan in his early years and engaged in revolutionary work. In the 16th year of the Republic, he served as the Shanghai General Commander. Mr. Zhang Jun Guang Xiao Ying

He made great contributions to the recapture of Shanghai. Later, he fought in the Jianghuai area, serving as a division and brigade commander. After the Jinan Incident, he returned to Shanghai in anger, dedicating himself to mass movements, such as the dockworkers' union, the United Party Affairs Committee, the Chinese Benevolent Association, and as a member of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. He is currently the Standing Director and Chairman of the National Federation of National Salvation Organizations.

Mr. Tu's Conversation 112

A reporter asked Mr. Tu Liang, the Secretary-General of the association, about the circumstances before his disappearance. According to him, Mr. Zhang was amiable and treated people with sincerity. He adhered to the "Four Don'ts" – no prostitution, no gambling, no smoking, and no deception – and often advised his friends accordingly. On the 27th morning, I (Tu himself) had a conversation with Mr. Zhang for about an hour, during which he expressed his extreme heartache over the loss of the Northeast for more than a year. He relied on the volunteer army to maintain the situation, but they were gradually running out of strength, and Rehe was in danger, Japanese goods were being dumped. If they didn't intensify their efforts to support the volunteer army and stir up public excitement, the future would be unimaginable. Mr. Zhang was always courageous and resolute in his actions. This sudden disappearance is likely due to enemy machinations. He hoped all sectors would rise up to rescue him, to avoid repeating the tragedy of Xiang Songmao, and so on.

The members asked the chairman to be responsible for handling them. 6) Jin Liren proposed that the association should stipulate a regular meeting date and publicly decide to hold an executive committee meeting once a month to discuss various proposals. The meeting was adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Labor Strike at Lulin Pond Hinders Hunan Goods from Arriving in Shanghai 120

Lulin Pond in Hunan is an important location for transporting Hunan goods. This winter, the water level in Hunan has receded, and riverboats cannot travel there, but there are many goods being exported. Various shipping companies have sent tugboats to carry them. However, last week, the dockworkers at the port demanded higher wages, but the management refused. The workers united and went on strike, stopping the loading and unloading of goods. As a result, shipping between Hunan and Shanghai has also been affected.

Rushing to Load Merchandise: Merchants usually rush to load and clear all goods before the end of the lunar year to close out the year. Merchants who have ordered Hunan goods are sending more tugboats to compete to transport them to Shanghai. Therefore, various shipping companies in Shanghai have increased the number of iron barges on the Hunan-Shanghai route and sent them to Lulin Pond to load goods for transport. China Merchants, San Bei, Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and others have all sent shallow-water boats to Changsha to load bulk grains.

Detaining Ships Dispute: When various shipping companies' tugboats arrived at Lulin to load goods, a labor strike occurred. The merchants, due to time constraints, could not delay for long, so they obtained the consent of the various shipping companies and ordered the iron barges to sail to Huangmaotan to hire workers to load. However, this provoked resistance from the striking workers, who united with armed comrades and seized China Merchants San Bei Company's barge No. 8, forcibly detaining it and preventing it from loading. Other companies' boats arriving at Lulin were also detained, causing a major dispute.

Petitioning for a Government Office: Since the various shipping companies' barges were detained and goods could not be unloaded, the merchants became even more anxious. Yesterday, a telegram was sent stating that the Hunan branches of China Merchants and San Bei, together with representatives of the merchants, went to the Hunan Provincial Government to request a solution to stop the workers from detaining ships and obstructing transportation, so as not to hinder shipping, stop merchandise, and affect the market. The workers, upon receiving this news, also gathered at the government office to petition, putting forward their demands to counter the management. The unrest is currently escalating fiercely, and how it will be resolved is still unknown.

Banks and Money Houses to Close for New Year's Day 121

All financial and commercial establishments in Shanghai will be closed on New Year's Day, 1933, to celebrate. As the date approaches, it is urgent to make arrangements. It was heard yesterday that the money houses have already decided to close for New Year's Day and the 2nd, resuming business on the 3rd and handling collections and settlements as usual. However, the banks have not been able to reach a consensus. Some will close for three days, while others will follow the example of the money houses and close for two days. For example, the banks on the Bund must close for four days to make up for the Sunday holiday. Therefore, it is expected that the entire industry will not resume business until the 5th.

Two Railway Bureau Directors Hosted the Press Yesterday Afternoon 122

Reporting on the Current Situation and Improvement Plans

Huang Boqiao, the director of the Jinpu and Huning Railways, invited reporters from various newspapers and news agencies to the bureau's conference room at 2:00 PM yesterday to report on everything. About twenty reporters from various newspapers attended. Director Huang and Deputy Director Wu Shaozeng first reported, and then asked the reporters to contribute their opinions on the accumulated problems of the railway and the areas that should be improved, based on what they had heard and seen on weekdays. Director Huang personally answered them, and the meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. The reports of the two directors, Huang and Wu, are detailed below:

The Economic Situation of the Two Railways 123

Director Huang reported, "Since I took office according to the Ministry's orders, I have been faced with the aftermath of the severe damage to the two railways and the constant unrest within the bureau. Therefore, the work of dealing with and rectifying the situation has been very cumbersome. Therefore, I have not been able to personally meet with you on several occasions, and I sincerely apologize. Now that the major issues of the bureau have been resolved to a considerable extent, I have invited you here to report in detail. I am very honored that you have graciously accepted the invitation. The operations of the two railways were very difficult even before the January 28th Shanghai Incident, because the Jinpu Railway runs parallel to the Yangtze River. The January 28th Incident caused severe damage to the two railways. The bureau was burned down, and the railway property was damaged, resulting in a direct loss of more than 8.93 million yuan and an indirect loss of more than 5.67 million yuan, totaling more than 14.6 million yuan. After the incident, on the one hand, the cost of restoration and reorganization was enormous, and on the other hand, the market was depressed and credit was extremely tight, resulting in sluggish operations and a sharp decline in revenue. The difficulties and crises of the two railways have become even more severe. Taking the major responsibilities of the two railways as an example, as of the end of November this year, the debt to the Sino-British Syndicate for principal and interest is more than 8 million yuan, the debt for the purchase of vehicles is more than 4 million yuan, the debt to Guangzhou-Kowloon is more than 200,000 yuan, and Huning owes

Another Import of Japanese Fishing Boats 124

Price cuts and Dumping Disrupt the Market

According to the Central News Agency, the Japanese fishing boat Osprey Maru imported twice last month, selling its catches from fishing in China's territorial waters in the Chinese market and taking the profits away. It is now reported that the Japanese fishing boat imported again on the 25th, bringing in 1,100 boxes of yellow croaker, shark, eel, etc., weighing more than 30,000 catties. To avoid attracting attention from the Chinese, the ship berthed at Yangshupu and used barges to transport the goods in, entrusting Yongmao and Shenfeng Vegetable and Fruit Shops in the 16th Concession to sell them. At that time, the price of domestic fresh bucket-headed yellow croaker was around 14 yuan per dan, while the yellow croaker imported by the Japanese fishing boat was initially priced at 6 to 8 yuan per dan, a price cut and dumping that disrupted the fish market.

Outstanding loan of more than 1.8 million yuan, for a total debt of more than 14 million yuan, a staggering amount. The routine operating expenses of the two railways alone require more than 630,000 yuan per month for wages. In November this year, the balance of income and expenses was still short of more than 900,000 yuan. It is now the end of December, and everything needs to be paid for, but the two railways currently have only more than 420,000 yuan in funds, which is still short of 210,000 yuan even if used entirely for wages. As for the plans for the restoration and reorganization of the two railways, including repairing bridges, building docks, adding locomotives and freight cars, replacing sleepers and steel rails, relocating and expanding various machine shops and stations, and the equipment that the bureau should add after the completion of the ferry project between Xiaguan and Pukou next year, the cost of all these is difficult to estimate. If we do not urgently raise funds, there is no hope of progress, and even maintaining the status quo will be impossible.

Future Efforts 125

As for future efforts, abstractly speaking, there are several aspects: 1) Railways are a national transportation agency, and everything must be based on serving the people. Therefore, in the future, we must eliminate all unreasonable habits and make them conform to commercialization. 2) Railways are a specialized business that requires various technical personnel everywhere, and there can be no compromise. Unless it is actually urgently needed, we will never lightly appoint anyone. Even if the business increases and we have no choice but to add people, we must conduct strict assessments, selecting people for the job and gradually not selecting jobs for people. 3) Finances must be transparent. The only way to save the two railways after the devastation is to actively increase revenue and passively save expenses. For debts, we must repay the principal and pay interest on time, without causing delays. All expenditures must be made public, and simple forms showing the financial status of each department must be prepared and made public to all colleagues of the two railways. There must be no ambiguity or perfunctoriness, so that funds are not wasted and things are done practically. 4) Actively build and improve efficiency. In addition to quickly reorganizing the damaged parts of the railway, we must actively carry out other new businesses that are related to the future development of the two railways according to the economic situation of the two railways, so that they are rationalized and commercialized. No matter what the situation, we must strive forward and not stop until we achieve our goals. Other equipment in the bureau is of great importance to work efficiency. For example, there are currently 66 locomotives, but two-thirds of them have no depot to store them, and they are exposed all day long, resulting in huge losses. Most of the workers are also working outdoors, which reduces their efficiency significantly. In the future, we will add equipment as needed to avoid the above-mentioned losses.

The Addition of a Deputy Director 126

At the beginning of my tenure, the Ministry of Railways also added a deputy director to assist me. Since the implementation of responsible transportation on this railway, the amount of work has doubled, and we are constantly researching and improving. Deputy Director Wu is proficient in railway cost accounting and railway management, and can cooperate and work hard, making it easier to cope with the situation. Moreover, the two railways are by no means satisfied with the status quo, and are urgently seeking reform and improvement, such as: 1) Extending the railway, planning to extend it westward from Nanjing to enter Anhui and Jiangxi, and eastward to extend the railway to Wusong, so that the products of the interior can directly reach the port and be sold to the world. 2) The ferry across the Yangtze River between Tianjin-Pukou and Jinpu Railways will be completed by the spring and summer of next year. At that time, the transportation of the two railways can be directly reached. After the completion of the above two facilities, the railway business will also increase many times. Therefore, the addition of a deputy director will greatly benefit the reform of the railway and the revitalization of the business.

Deputy Director Wu's Speech 127

After Director Huang's report, Deputy Director Wu made a report, saying that he had been ordered to assist Director Huang and would follow him and work together. The increase in current bureau affairs can be summarized in several points: 1) Responsible for transportation, 2) Important position, 3) Reorganizing debts, 4) Connecting all departments to achieve the effect of division of labor and cooperation, 5) Investigating various freight rates to seek reform. All of the above are the efforts that must be made in the future, especially the fifth item of investigating various freight rates, which is more complicated and important. The convenience of water transportation is increasing, and the construction of highways is also actively underway. The railway's business is mainly freight transportation. However, merchants try to avoid high costs to reduce costs. If the bureau can reduce freight rates, merchants will be happy to choose it. After Deputy Director Wu's report, reporters made many suggestions and criticisms about the accumulated problems of the bureau and the areas that should be reformed. Director Huang answered them one by one.

Companies Not Registered Must Register by the Deadline 133

The National Federation of Commerce and Industry Received a Notice from the Ministry of Industry

The National Federation of Commerce and Industry received a notice from the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating that according to Article 18 of the General Rules for Merchants, commercial establishments may not use the words "company" or similar words in their names unless they are operated as companies. This also applies to those who take over the business of a company and continue to operate it as a company. Furthermore, according to Article 5 of the Company Law, a company may not be established until it has been registered with the competent authorities in the location of its main store. In addition, according to Article 114 of the same law, a company may not issue shares until it has been registered. Furthermore, Article 231, paragraphs 1 and 6, of the same law stipulates penalties for those who do not apply for registration or illegally issue shares. Therefore, a company may not be established and may not issue shares unless it is organized in accordance with the law and has been approved for registration. Recently, it has been found that a small number of merchants in well-known provinces and cities are engaged in business, or are not organized as companies, but falsely use the name of a company, or are organized under the name of a public entity, but do not apply for registration. They should be banned according to the law. Companies that are not registered have not obtained the status of a legal person, and the type of organization has not been determined. They often call themselves limited companies, but because they are not registered, they must bear unlimited liability to the outside world. It is clear that they started business first, but because they are not registered, they cannot prevent others from imitating their brand names. The company itself suffers a lot of harm, and the directors must bear heavier responsibility. Although it is understandable that registration is delayed due to unclear procedures or inconvenient transportation, it is still not in accordance with the law. Therefore, we hereby issue another notice that all companies established in the future should apply for registration in accordance with the time limit stipulated in Article 5 of the Company Law. Those companies that have already been established but have not yet applied for registration must all apply for registration in accordance with the law before June 30th of the Republic of China. If they still fail to comply after the deadline, they will be punished immediately according to the law. Furthermore, according to Article 31 of the Company Law Implementation Regulations, after a company is registered, its registration certificate will be issued by the Ministry of Industry. According to Article 5 of the current Company Registration Rules, company registration must be confirmed after the Ministry of Industry approves and issues the certificate. Therefore, the application for registration by the company must be finally approved and issued a certificate by the Ministry in order to be considered confirmed and have legal effect. In addition to distributing and publishing the announcement in the newspaper for public knowledge, the Federation is hereby notified to inform all chambers of commerce to abide by it. This notice is hereby given.

Land Bureau Announcement: Owners Must Be Present During Land Survey 134

Must Fill in the Location and Boundaries in Detail During the Survey

The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau announces: In order to announce the matter, it is necessary for the owner to clearly fill in the location and boundaries of the household land when the bureau handles land survey cases, and after the date of the land survey notice, first come to the bureau to contact the location for waiting, so that the surveyor can go to the survey together. It is now found that some owners do not fill in the four boundaries of the household land, or do not contact after receiving the notice, or entrust others to act as agents, so that the boundary cannot be indicated during the survey, and there is no way to measure. There are also owners who change the communication address and fail to report the correction, so the notice cannot be delivered and is delayed. The people feel that the delay is annoying, and the bureau also feels annoyed. In order to facilitate the progress of the business, it is specially announced that the owner must fill in the household land in detail, confirm the communication address, and report to the bureau if the communication address has been changed. After receiving the land survey notice, you must come to the bureau in person to contact and wait for the location. Do not entrust others to act as agents. This is a matter of property rights, so do not delay yourself. This is announced on December 28th, 21st year of the Republic of China. Director Jin Liren.

Household Registration Plates to be Issued to Chinese Residents Starting Next Year 135

General Residents Take Note: Violations Will Be Penalized

The Municipal Police Bureau, regarding residents within the boundaries, stipulates that whenever a household moves into or out of the Chinese territory, they must first register with the relevant district office and obtain an investigation certificate. However, residents often lose these certificates. Therefore, the bureau has decided to switch to household registration plates starting January 15th of next year. These plates will be affixed to the doors of each household, preventing loss and facilitating inspections. The regulations for issuing household registration plates are as follows: "Regulations for Issuing Household Registration Plates (Article 1: The issuance of household registration plates in this city shall be managed by the Police Bureau in accordance with these regulations. (Article 2) The household registration plate in this city serves as the basis for random checks of the population and reporting of changes. (Article 3) The outer frame and bracket of the household registration plate will be made of enamel, measuring ten centimeters in height and eleven centimeters in width. The entire plate will have a blue background with the words "Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau Household Registration Plate" written horizontally in white. The plate will be covered with glass and contain a piece of paper with the address, house number, name of the head of household, occupation, age, place of origin, and number of family members. (Article 4) Household registration will be based on the household unit. Except for government agencies affiliated with the National Government, all other residents, shops, and private factories, hospitals, banks, schools, etc., must be registered. (Article 5) Each set of household registration plates will cost three silver dollars for production. After registration, a receipt will be issued and collected by the police officers dispatched by the district office. The fee will be paid by the landlord or the second landlord.

Page 12

Those who refuse to pay will be fined three silver dollars. However, if the landlord does not reside in the property, the tenant may pay in advance and deduct the amount from the rent upon payment. (Article 6) Only the Police Bureau has the right to manufacture and issue household registration plates in this city. Any unauthorized manufacturing or affixing will be penalized with a fine of three silver dollars. (Article 7) After the household registration plate is affixed, both the landlord and tenant are responsible for its safekeeping. The writing on the plate must not be allowed to become blurred. If the glass on the plate is broken, the household must replace it themselves. If the metal frame is damaged or lost, the district office must be notified immediately, and the Police Bureau must be notified to remake and re-affix the plate, for which a fee of four jiao will be charged. If the paper inside the plate is damaged, the damaged paper must be submitted to the district office to apply for a replacement, for which a fee of three fen will be charged. Failure to report will result in a fine of two silver dollars. This restriction does not apply in cases of genuine disasters that could not have been prevented. (Article 8) After the household registration plate is affixed, it becomes the private property of the landlord. When a tenant moves out, they may not take it with them. However, tenants may purchase their own. (Article 9) If any changes occur in the household, the paper inside the plate must be taken out, reported to the district office, and a fee of three fen paid to apply for a replacement paper, which must be re-inserted. Failure to comply with this procedure will result in a fine of two silver dollars upon inspection. If the landlord knows and fails to report, they will be subject to the same penalty. (Article 10) When residents move, whether within the city or out of the city, they must submit the paper inside the household registration plate to their district office to obtain a relocation certificate or a move-out certificate, free of charge. Failure to comply with this procedure will result in a fine of two silver dollars upon discovery. If the landlord knows and fails to report, they will be subject to the same penalty. (Article 11) Matters not covered in these regulations may be amended at any time. (Article 12) These regulations shall come into effect upon approval by the Municipal Government."

Measures for Disaster Victims in Jiangwan to Borrow Money to Build Houses 136

The Municipal Government Approves Loans to be Issued in Three Installments Starting January of Next Year; Municipal Bank Has Already Raised 40,000 Yuan

The Municipal Government previously instructed the Police Bureau, Public Works Bureau, and Accounting Bureau to review and propose measures regarding the petition of disaster victims in the Jiangwan district to raise funds for building houses. The bureaus have now submitted a report stating, "Regarding the joint petition, we are submitting this matter for review. The Jiangwan district disaster victims petitioned for relief, and we were ordered to review and handle the matter. We drafted four measures and jointly submitted them to the government for review. On the 4th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Headquarters of the War Zone Relief Committee stating that the first, second, and third measures proposed by our bureau and others have been approved. We were instructed to take note, etc. We have already dispatched personnel to conduct on-site surveys starting on the 30th of last month, and we held two meetings on December 9th and 14th to decide on the following measures: (1) According to the report of the municipal committee members, there are 1,015 households of disaster victims who should be provided with houses. After our bureau decided on the classification, we re-checked the original household registers and excluded those who had already built houses or had more than one remaining room that could provide temporary shelter. There are 850 households urgently awaiting housing, which matches the previous estimate of 850 households. The name lists of all households building houses and the brief lists of the number of houses to be built in each village have been compiled and submitted. (2) The Local Maintenance Committee has agreed to use 31,000 yuan for building houses for disaster victims in Jiangwan. However, the committee is still building houses on behalf of the victims, not providing funds for self-construction. In order to meet the needs of the disaster victims and avoid profiteering by middlemen, our bureau decided to provide loans in installments for construction. Since the construction methods are different, it is difficult to merge the two approaches. We decided that 202 households of disaster victims in Jian 28 Tu, Jian 22 Tu, Jian 35 Tu, Jian 26 Tu, and Jian 34 Tu will be built by the Local Maintenance Committee. The remaining 648 households will be provided with loans from the city to build houses, requiring a total of 97,200 yuan. In addition to the original 20,080 yuan war zone housing loan, an additional 69,200 yuan is needed. (3) The Local Maintenance Committee built more than 100 rooms in the Jing Miao Civilian Village. Our bureau previously planned to use the existing houses to relocate 150 nearby disaster-stricken households. However, because the houses in the Civilian Village are not suitable for farmers to live in, the Public Works Bureau approved a notice from the Shanghai War Zone Relief Committee to request a joint inspection with the Security Department. If it can be used for other purposes, the government will raise funds to purchase it. We have dispatched personnel to conduct a joint inspection and found that it can be used as a barracks. The Public Works Bureau has jointly submitted a separate report to the governor for review. If the village houses are suitable for use as barracks, the purchase price can be allocated from the aforementioned 69,200 yuan. We will also instruct the municipal committee members to negotiate with the Local Maintenance Committee. If the sale price can be handled by the government, it can be incorporated into the remaining housing loans. If the Maintenance Committee still intends to allocate it themselves, they can allocate a portion of the 648 households to be built in this city at a rate of 150 yuan per household. Assuming the sale price of the Civilian Village is 20,000 yuan, if the committee needs to build it themselves, then in addition to the allocated 30,000 yuan, 200 households will be allocated to the committee for handling. This city will only need to prepare loans for 448 households. (4) According to the previous report, we requested the government to allocate 46,000 yuan, totaling 105,000 yuan, for the construction of 700 houses. At that time, we originally planned to accommodate 150 households in the Civilian Village. Now that the Civilian Village needs to be purchased for use by the Security Department, the required funds have also increased. According to the current number of households, the city treasury, including the purchase price of the Civilian Village, will raise 69,200 yuan, which is sufficient for allocation. However, the severe winter is approaching, and the people are in urgent need of rescue. The loan cannot be delayed. We plan to issue the loan in three installments on January 1st, 15th, and 31st. The first and second installments will account for two-thirds of the total 97,200 yuan, totaling 64,800 yuan. In addition to the war zone's temporary relief loan for housing construction in Jiangwan, which can be allocated first, an additional 36,800 yuan is needed. We request the government to raise and allocate the funds as soon as possible to cope with the situation. The remaining 30,000 yuan can be allocated after the charity event ends. (5) Regarding the loan method, our bureau believes that since the relief funds come from the city treasury, we should be extremely frugal and strive to benefit the disaster victims. Therefore, after conducting a household survey, we carefully drafted the loan method and plan to distribute it in three installments to prevent the loan from being diverted to other uses and failing to achieve the actual construction of houses. We plan to first compile a list of households approved for loans after a joint review with the Municipal Committee and announce it to the public. Then, the Municipal War Zone Temporary Relief Loan Office will supervise the Jiangwan District Municipal Committee members in handling the loan matters. We will prepare loan vouchers and issue them clearly to the approved households. The vouchers will be submitted to the General Loan Office for verification and issuance. When distributing the second and third installment vouchers, the municipal committee members should verify the construction progress of the household and indicate it separately before signing and issuing. Those who do not start construction after receiving the first installment of the loan will have their rights to the second and third installments of the loan revoked, and this will be indicated on the first installment loan voucher. Whether all the personnel dispatched for on-site surveys and meeting decisions are feasible, we hereby submit this together with the Jiangwan District disaster victim roster and the number of houses to be built for the governor's review and request that the Finance Bureau be ordered to raise and allocate the funds in advance and swiftly issue instructions. This is for the public good." The Municipal Government, based on the report, believes that the proposed measures are feasible and that the required funds have been discussed with the Municipal Bank, which has provided 40,000 yuan to meet the needs. Therefore, it has instructed the bureaus to comply and handle the matter properly, and has also ordered the Finance Bureau to handle it jointly.

Captains' Association Reports on the Circumstances of the Sinking of the New Fu Tai 139

Regarding the news of the sinking of the New Fu Tai, a report was also received by the Chinese Merchant Marine Captains' Association at 38 Avenue Edward VII in this port and published as follows: (1) The location of the accident was HengtCbick Island, located at 30 degrees 42 minutes 45 seconds north latitude and 122 degrees 2 minutes 55 seconds east longitude. The entire crew of the ship consisted of 42 people. The captain and first mate were Russian, and the second mate was Chinese. Whether they had certificates of competency from the Ministry of Communications and whether they were legally qualified to serve as crew members is subject to investigation before a determination can be made. The island is a few feet above sea level and is not a reef. The nautical chart also indicates its location, so the accident was unexpected. The ship sank half an hour after hitting the island, and the current swept it to about 2 cables south of the island. The hull is completely submerged, with only the mast and chimney visible. (2) The Tong Shun rescued the survivors. The Tong Shun was carrying coal from Hongqi to Nanjing. At 10:00 a.m. on the 26th, while passing near Daji Mountain, it received telegrams from the Tongsha pilot boat and the patrol office. It immediately turned back to rescue the survivors. The Zhengji Company's Hui An also accompanied it. In the afternoon, it arrived at the scene of the accident and saw that the ship had sunk. The Tong Shun circled around Tripoint Island and N·W·Horn, sounding its whistle to indicate that a ship had come to help. At 4:00 p.m., someone was finally seen on the top of Liaochu Mountain waving clothes, indicating the location of the stranded crew members. However, it was already dark, and the evening wind was strong, so it was impossible to move forward. It anchored and waited. At dawn on the 27th, it lowered lifeboat No. 3 and sailed to the island. Fishermen rushed to tell them and guided them to the stranded crew members. A total of 20 people were rescued, including 3 who had died. Only 17 survivors were left. So, they shared life and death together, boarded the boat, and were transferred to the Tong Shun and returned to Shanghai. (3) The Hui An left. The captain and vice-captain of the Zhengji Company's Hui An were Japanese. When they sailed to the scene of the accident with the Tong Shun, they immediately turned around and sailed away upon seeing that the New Fu Tai had already sunk. They did not care about rescuing the survivors at all. (4) The captain was incompetent. The weather was clear when the ship hit the island. The accident was entirely due to the Russian captain's unfamiliarity with the route. The island is quite high above the water and can be seen from a distance. The so-called reef and fog are excuses to cover up the truth. (5) Post-accident policy. Finally, the executive committee of the association said that in previous years, accidents involving Chinese ships were caused by foreign crew members making unintentional mistakes, which could not be saved by human effort. However, Chinese shipowners worship foreigners. Although there are more and more Chinese crew members in recent years, and talents are emerging, they are still unwilling to hire them. The reason behind this is difficult to explain in a few words. However, not all foreign crew members are good materials. Recently, a certain ship sailing from Shanghai to Haizhou, with a Russian captain, spent three days and nights near Entering Gong Island and could not find the port of Haizhou. This is a big joke in the maritime world. However, this matter has not been exposed, so the Ministry of Communications and the Maritime Affairs Bureau have not thoroughly investigated it, and the shipowners have also not expressed their opinions. Therefore, unless the competent authorities take early action to eliminate the bad ones, and still allow shipowners to freely hire foreign crew members, future losses will be inevitable.

Minutes of the 127th Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Lawyers Association 142

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its 127th joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committee at 7:00 p.m. last night at its offices located at the intersection of Route Belles and Route Ratard in the French Concession. The committee members present were Zhou Shi, Lu Dingkui, Chen Rui, Zhu Fu Jiu, Jiang Jiemin, Tang Hao, Shen Jun Ru, Zhang Zhengxue, Li Shirui, etc. Lu Dingkui served as chairman, and Dai Jixian served as recorder. The proposed motions are recorded as follows: (1) The Ministry of Judicial Administration of the National Government replied in a telegram stating that it agreed with the Association's deleted telegram proposal. However, the adoption of the jury system concerns individual judicial issues and cannot be decided without a comprehensive study of the overall situation. (Resolution) Another telegram will be sent to explain the pros and cons of the jury system, requesting the Ministry of Judicial Administration to adopt it. Committee member Li Shirui was nominated to draft the text. (2) Member Ying Jirong sent a letter to prove that Dai Peiyuan did not impersonate a lawyer. (Resolution) This case will be handed over to the Supervisory Committee for investigation. (3) Member Jin Hongji replied in a letter that he did not insult Lawyer Ma Chang. (Resolution) The original letter will be forwarded to member Ma Chang for reference. (4) The Shanghai District Court replied that it has always uniformly accepted formally submitted pleadings. (Resolution) It will be forwarded to all members for reference. (5) Member Hu Chongji sent a letter requesting discussion on whether a petition fee of 7 jiao 5 fen should be paid in addition to the 1 jiao judicial stamp fee for the application to inspect the case file. (Resolution) A letter will be sent to the Jiangsu Second Branch Court and the First Special District Court to request a reply. (6) The Shanghai Local Association sent a statistical letter requesting the provision of materials. (Resolution) It will be handed over to the Standing Committee for appropriate handling. (7) Shanghai Private Wudan Elementary School reported that it was forced to close down by the French authorities and requested that the Association uphold justice and provide assistance. (Resolution) The school will be informed to report to the Shanghai Education Bureau and protest to the French Municipal Council. (8) Committee member Tang Hao submitted the review opinions and proposed additions and deletions to the Association's rules of procedure and accounting methods for discussion. (Resolution) It should be transcribed, printed, and distributed to all committee members for review at the next meeting. (9) Committee member Tang Hao proposed that the Shanghai Second Special District Court be requested to instruct the French Concession Patrol to allow lawyers to visit detainees at any time. (Resolution) Passed and will be implemented accordingly. (10) Lawyers Huang Zhongyue, Huang Neng Cong, Su Shi, Lu Ming, Ma Jiazhen, Li Chunsen, Wang Man Juan, Fang Junjie, Hou Ce, Chen Yixiang, Fang Ren, Rong Zhenlong, Jia Zhen, Zhuang Zhenfu, Chen Rong, and others applied for membership. Expanding the Publicity for the Monthly Donation Campaign and the Charity Performance for Northeast Refugees 143

Including the "Flower Queen Dance Election" Event

The charity performance for Northeast refugees, hosted by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and others, held at the New World, has been open for twelve days. In line with its purpose of promoting relief for the Northeast and advocating for the monthly donation campaign, new methods are being implemented from time to time. The following is a record of the latest news from last night:

Free Admission to the Exhibition Area for Promotional Materials: In order to concentrate the power of enthusiastic people from the middle class and below, the association has specially established a method for free admission to the exhibition area for promotional materials, in order to expand the monthly donation campaign and achieve practical results. The methods are as follows: ㈠ Dates: January 4th to January 8th, ㈡ Time: 10:00 AM to 2:00 PM daily, ㈢ Exhibits: (A) Painful paintings from the Art Academy, (B) Fragmented map of the Northeast, (C) Appeals from beyond the Great Wall on the wall, (D) Tragic scenes of the Jiangqiao battle, (E) Heartbreaking model of Zhabei, (F) Heroic plaster statues, (G) Feasible national salvation plan, (H) Relaxing exhibition of seasonal flowers, ㈣ Conditions: (A) Holders of bank monthly donation receipts of one jiao or more of silver dollars before December 31st, 1932 (upon arrival, Boy Scouts will exchange them for free admission tickets), (B) Those who voluntarily donate two jiao or more of silver dollars per month after New Year's Day of 1933 (those who pay will receive a receipt from the Boy Scouts), (C) Schools, labor unions, factories, and companies with 50 or more people must submit a formal letter to the association one day in advance to register and receive free admission forms, (D) Visitors must fill out a registration form, which can be clipped from advertisements in major newspapers today.

Additional Rules for the Flower Queen Dance Election: In addition to the dance stars and basic dance girls from major dance halls coming to the dance floor to provide voluntary dance partners every day, the association originally planned to have enthusiastic famous flowers accompany the dance on the four evenings of the 24th, 25th of this month, last night, and New Year's Day next year to serve the country. The dance tickets earned, with each ticket worth 1.5 yuan, will be included in the flower election calculation. Now, famous flowers who are enthusiastic about accompanying dances voluntarily give up their voting rights from dance tickets, so that famous flowers who are not familiar with dancing will not reduce their courage to compete as a result, so that adding one more vote to the election power means adding one more point to the national salvation strength. The association appreciates their enthusiasm and has specially formulated a method for the Flower Queen Dance Election. The simple rules are as follows: ㈡ The first place winner with the most voting rights from dance tickets by 2:00 AM on New Year's Day will be crowned the Flower Queen and presented with a large silver trophy. ㈡ The second place winner will be crowned the Flower Queen's East Palace and presented with a number two silver trophy. ㈢ The third place winner will be crowned the Flower Queen's Fourth Palace and presented with a number three silver trophy. ㈣ Those who obtain 2,500 or more dance ticket votes (i.e., 500 jiao) will all be crowned Flower Dance Stars and presented with a small silver trophy each. ㈤ Those who obtain 250 or more votes (i.e., 50 yuan) will each be presented with a commemorative certificate. ㈥ Flower Queen dance tickets are converted into votes, with each dance ticket worth one yuan counting as five votes.

Existing Results of the Flower Queen Dance Election: Looking at the results of the famous flowers participating in the Flower Queen Dance Election on the 24th and 25th, Xue Mei has 4,254 votes, Bing Xin has 3,923 votes, Ying Jiao has 3,372 votes, Lin Xiaoyun has 3,124 votes, and Ying Chun has 2,582 votes. All five of these individuals have exceeded the qualifications in Article 4. Xue You, Bing Hua, and Xue Fei all have more than 2,000 votes, while Qing Lou and Qin Fang all have more than 1,500 votes. It is unknown who will win the title of Flower Queen in the final calculation on New Year's Day night.

Special Programs After New Year's Day: The association's performance program was originally scheduled until New Year's Day, but it has now been extended to the 8th. Shanghai West Rickshaws Will Collect a Vehicle Donation of Five Jiao Per Month 144

To Be Implemented Starting January Next Year

The Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities and Finance Bureaus jointly issued a notice stating: Regarding the matter of a joint notice, after investigation, the operating range of business rickshaws in Shanghai West is limited to the four districts of Fahua, Caojing, Hongqiao, and Zhenru. The vehicle donation rate seems difficult to match with those running throughout the city. It is now proposed to collect a vehicle donation of five jiao per vehicle per month, following the precedent of vehicles running in Pudong or Wusong, in order to show fairness. This has been submitted by our bureau, etc., to the Municipal Government's Order No. 4267, which states: "The joint report is understood and approved as proposed. You are instructed to comply with this order," and so on. In addition to sending a letter to the Public Security Bureau instructing its subordinates to assist and issue orders, a notice is hereby issued to the owners of business rickshaws in Shanghai West, requiring them to pay the vehicle donation at the Municipal Finance Bureau's West Shanghai Tax Collection Office starting from January 1, 1933, with the temporary vehicle permit issued by this Public Utilities Bureau.
