A Country Girl from Huzhou Was Sold to Shanghai 145

After Explaining the Situation, the Employer Realized They Had Been Deceived and Sent the Country Girl to the Jiliang Institute

Chen Meizhen, a 17-year-old country girl from Xinshi Township, Huzhou, had beautiful features. Her parents died early, and she was poor and had no one to rely on. Through a matchmaker, she was betrothed to the surname Zhao family in the same village as a child bride. Her husband's name was Zhao Qian, and at the age of 21, he had not yet had a wedding ceremony, but his family was also not well-off, working hard every day. On the 11th day of the 11th lunar month, two people from the same village, named Ding Kui and A Xiang, who ran a small pharmacy, were local playboys. Seeing the girl's charming appearance, they lured her and brought her to Shanghai, colluding with a fugitive Tanglou woman, using the excuse of introducing her as a helper, and staying at Dai Hua's house, a Hangzhou woman who played cards at No. 6 Guangxi Road. Between the 26th of this month, she was sold to Wu Zhang, a Suzhou woman at No. 34 Yalu Road, as a niece-in-law, for a total of 180 yuan. Wu Zhang was very pleased with the girl's gentle and elegant demeanor and treated her very well, even changing her into new clothes. Although the girl was young, she knew the difference between right and wrong. She immediately stated to Wu Zhang that she was a married woman and had been deceived and abducted to Shanghai. Once discovered, it would definitely implicate her. Wu Zhang was greatly alarmed upon hearing this and immediately asked someone to deceive Hua and go to her residence to question her about the girl's origins. Hua did not know that she had been exposed by the girl and falsely claimed that Chen Meizhen was her daughter. Because her family was poor, she was willing to marry her niece as an adopted daughter, and nothing else would happen. She also rebuked the girl, saying, "You don't know what's good for you. You have plenty of food and clothing here, and you still want to go to heaven?" The girl angrily said that her parents had already passed away one after another, and that Hua was not her biological mother, so why would she say such a thing? They argued with each other, but Dai Hua was still not fully aware and comforted the girl slightly, saying, "You should stay here peacefully and not leave lightly." Wu Zhang also inquired about the truth from the girl and found out that only 80 yuan of the bride price had been paid, and the deception was not too deep. So, she reported it to the Hongkou Patrol Room a few days ago, and the detective, Sun Aizhong, and the patrolman, Li Zexing, secretly arrested Dai Hua and brought her to the patrol room. Yesterday morning, she was escorted to the Criminal Court No. 3 of the First Special District Court. The patrol room lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, explained the whole story and requested a postponement. Subsequently, the girl, Chen Meizhen, explained the whole process, while the employer, Wu Zhang, stated that her husband's name was Wen Guang, a Cantonese, and he was an accountant on a certain ship. She had a nephew who was just over twenty years old and eager to marry. She wanted to find a wife and was entrusting someone to do so. At that time, her husband's friend, Wu Shilian, and the Cantonese woman, Chen Bagu, acted as matchmakers and told the defendant that they would marry her daughter to her nephew as a child bride for a bride price of 180 yuan. She would temporarily join the family as a child bride. Who knew that she was an abducted girl? Fortunately, Chen Meizhen told her the truth, otherwise, she would have been implicated endlessly. Now, she has only been deceived out of a bride price of 80 yuan. Wu Xuelian and Chen Bagu testified that they did not know the defendant and that this girl's origins were the doing of the fugitive dwarf woman and the defendant. They did not know the details. When questioned, the defendant stammered and said that the silver dollars had been taken away by the dwarf woman, requesting judgment. Judge Shen Bingrong examined the confessions and ordered that she be remanded in custody, rescheduled for investigation and further questioning. The girl, Chen Meizhen, was temporarily sent to the Jiliang Institute for care.

Record of the Interrogation of Liu Chongwu and Others from the Blood Vengeance Anti-Treason Group 155

Six Individuals Including Tang Shoukang Acquitted and Released

Liu Chongwu and Others Face Four Charges

The Court Examines Each Case Separately to Avoid Confusion

The Interrogation Continued Until Noon Yesterday Without Completion

Liu Chongwu and others, members of the Blood Vengeance Anti-Treason Group specializing in targeting smugglers and treacherous merchants, were arrested by Deputy Detective Zhao Bingkun of the Public Concession Police Department for repeatedly throwing bombs, opening fire, and injuring treacherous merchants and their employees. After thorough investigation, those with solid evidence were prosecuted in the First Special District Court, while those with slight suspicion were released on bail pending further investigation. Details have been previously reported. Yesterday morning was the scheduled hearing. The police sent the eight detainees, including Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, Tian Shuiyang, Zhang Linxiang, Fan Xisheng, Zhu Erkang, and Hua Zhida, along with five confiscated pistols and dozens of bullets, to the Second Tribunal of the First Special District Court. Tang Chou Kang, Wu Ligang, Xu Weizu, and the woman Pan Huizhu, who had been released on bail, and witnesses were also summoned to court. Defense lawyers Chen Tingrui, Xue Jiaqi, and Ruan Dingkui, and prosecuting lawyer Wang Yaotang from the police department, also appeared in court. At 11:00 AM, Judge Qian Wenji began the investigation. By 12:15 PM, it was not even halfway through, so it was postponed. The details of the interrogation are as follows:

Six Individuals Acquitted and Released　Tang Chou Kang, Wu Ligang, Xu Weizu, Pan Huizhu, and the detained Zhang Linxiang and Fan Xisheng, a total of six men and women, were found by the police to have no connection to the cases committed by the Anti-Treason Group. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that Tang and others had been wrongly accused, and since no evidence had been found, he requested that the six be acquitted and released first. Judge Qian approved the request, declared Tang and others not guilty, and released them in court. However, Pan Huizhu was instructed to remain in the courtroom in case her brother Pan Hongsheng's case required questioning.

First Examining Illegal Possession of Military Weapons　After Tang and others were released, only six defendants remained: Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, Tian Shuiyang, Zhu Erkang, and Hua Zhida. These six were charged with multiple counts, including conspiracy to murder, attempted murder, intimidation, and illegal possession of military weapons. The police lawyer proposed examining each case separately to avoid confusion and facilitate clarity. With the court's permission, the lawyer requested that the case of the defendants violating the regulations on banning military firearms be examined first, and described the circumstances of confiscating the pistols and bullets. Subsequently, Pannas, a Western official from the Public Works Department, detailed his examination of the pistols, bullets, and shell casings, stating that four of the five pistols had been used. He testified that the shell casings obtained in the Xinza Road and Hankou Road cases confirmed that they were fired from these four guns. He presented multiple photos of the guns and bullets along with the bullets themselves. Ge Leiboshi, the Western detective in charge of the case, reported the circumstances of finding the guns and bullets on or near the defendants. Liu Chongwu confessed that the pistol was given to him by Pan Hongsheng, while Pan Hongsheng and Cao Songshou both confessed that the pistols were issued by a fugitive named Gao. The other three, Tian, Zhu, and Hua, claimed that they did not carry pistols and did not know where they came from.

The Maotai Company Injury Case　Maotai Foreign Goods Store at 310 and 312 Xinza Road was bombed on November 18th, with the bombs failing to explode. Subsequently, shots were fired in the store, resulting in the death of manager Wang Jintang. The police investigation revealed that Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, Tian Shuiyang, and the fugitives Gao and Zhu were responsible. Therefore, Liu, Pan, Cao, and Tian were prosecuted for premeditated murder. According to the police lawyer, the defendants believed that Maotai Foreign Goods Store was illegally selling Japanese goods. On November 16th, they gathered at the Xinza Road Great King Temple to discuss countermeasures. Apart from Liu Chongwu, Pan, Cao, Tian, and the fugitives Gao and Zhu participated in the meeting. After the decision was made, Gao issued pistols to Pan and Cao, while Liu Chongwu and Zhu each carried a bomb. They set off from the Great King Temple to Maotai Store. Although Tian Shuiyang was unarmed, he was responsible for keeping watch. Upon arriving at Maotai's entrance, they found the store unloading goods, making it difficult to act. After the unloading, the defendants entered the store, and Liu threw the bomb, which did not explode. Cao Songshou and Zhu each fired a shot, wounding Wang Jintang. Although Pan Hongsheng also had a gun, he did not fire because he was keeping watch outside the store. The four defendants have confessed to this case at the police station, and Chinese and Western detectives took the four to Maotai to demonstrate the circumstances of the bombing and shooting. The evidence in this case is solid and complete, and they should be severely punished according to the law, the lawyer said. The Western deputy detective reported on the investigation process and presented two diaries found on Pan and Cao, as well as a photograph of them with Yun Enfang and Cai Yaozu. The lawyer stated that the diaries contained descriptions of the Maotai and other cases, as well as detailed addresses, contact information, and phone numbers of their accomplices. Ge Yongzhang, a partner at Maotai, testified that he was hiding in a corner due to extreme fear during the shooting and did not see the faces of the shooters. He stated that he witnessed the defendants signing their confessions at the police station. Liu Chongwu testified that he carried a bomb wrapped in newspaper outside the store. Cao Songshou and Gao entered the store pretending to buy cloth, and then he saw them exit. He threw the bomb in, but it did not explode because the safety mechanism was not activated. Cao Songshou testified that he fired a shot at the ground. Pan Hongsheng testified that they had repeatedly warned the store for selling enemy goods, but they did not repent. Their purpose was not to kill anyone. Tian Shuiyang testified that the action was decided on the spot and not pre-planned. At this point, lawyer Chen Tingrui and the police lawyer had some debate over the questions. Pan Hongsheng and Cao Songshou continued to testify that their purpose was purely to warn the treacherous merchants. They stated that treacherous merchants often hired red-shirted thugs to escort large quantities of Japanese goods during import, and if they interfered, they would be arrested and beaten by the red-shirt team. Therefore, they carried pistols for self-defense. At this point, all witnesses in the case had testified.

The Yuyuan Heng Injury Case　The police lawyer then presented the investigation into the Yuyuan Heng case, stating that the store was located at 339 Hankou Road. At 2:00 PM on November 24th, Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, and the fugitives Gao and Zhu went to the store and threw a bomb, injuring Wang, a store employee, who later died from his injuries, and another employee, who was still being treated in the hospital. The defendants had previously met at 263 Tianlu Road. Their original intention was to kill the store owner, Shen. Gao provided the pistols and bombs. Liu and Cao each held a pistol, while Pan and Shang each held a bomb. Therefore, Liu, Pan, and Cao were prosecuted for premeditated murder. Xu Genrong, a staff member of the store, testified that he heard a sudden noise and immediately fled, so he did not see who threw the bomb. Upon hearing this, Liu Chongwu claimed that Xu's statement was false. He stated that he entered the store first with the bomb and met Xu. He told Xu that the Northeast had fallen, and the volunteer army was fighting the Japanese invaders despite hunger and cold. He said that as merchants with conscience, they should completely awaken and stop selling enemy goods. If they only cared about personal interests, they were helping the tiger to hurt people. He said that instead of heeding the advice, Xu ordered the old bookkeeper standing aside to seize him. The bookkeeper bumped into the bomb he was holding, and the bomb fell to the ground. He then left the store, so he did not know if anyone was injured. Cao Songshou testified that he was in the alley and his pistol did not fire. It was an accidental discharge. Pan Hongsheng testified that he heard the gunshot, placed the bomb on the ground, and left.

The Sun Guangxing Bombing Case　The Sun Guangxing Clock Store at 133 Henan Road was bombed on October 24th by Pan Hongsheng and Cao Songshou, who also left a letter. The bomb exploded, injuring Xie, a Shaoxing man who was in the store to do business, in the back. He has now been treated at the hospital and was summoned to testify. The police lawyer stated the circumstances of the case and requested that Pan and Cao be punished for premeditated murder. Xie testified that the bomber was wearing green clothes and looked like Cao Songshou. Cao admitted it without hesitation, stating that the bomb and letter were given to him by someone named He. Pan claimed that he went along but was unarmed. It was already past noon, so Judge Qian adjourned the hearing to 1:00 PM on January 5th. The detectives took the defendants back to the police station for detention.

Four Kidnappers in the Wen Guohua Case Sentenced to Death 156

Wen Xuancheng, a native of Zhenjiang and the director of the Shanghai Middle School Association, lived at 2 Xiexing Lane, Haichao Road, in the city. His seven-year-old son, Guohua, was suddenly kidnapped outside his door on the 7th of last month, and a huge ransom was demanded. Later, Chief Detective You A'gen, Detective Liu Junqing, and Detectives Li Shugui and Pang Yutang of the Public Concession Police Station arrested twelve kidnappers, including Shen Wengao, Wan Shihhao, Yin Yucen, Lu Rongchang, Zhang Jun, Zhang Zhongshan, Zhu Xiaoguan, Wang Hongju, Guo Xibin, Xu Shengpu, Ding Guangzheng, and Wang Xijin. They confiscated one pistol and five bullets and rescued Wen Guohua at 110 Dixiwei Road. It was discovered that Shen Wengao and others had also committed the attempted kidnapping of Lu Ziqing, a comprador of Huada Foreign Firm, the shooting death of Lu, and four or five other major cases of kidnapping and robbery. After the First Special Court completed the interrogation, Chief Judge Ma Shide of the Criminal Court announced the verdict in Criminal Court One yesterday morning. Shen Wengao, Wan Shihhao, Yin Yucen, and Zhang Zhongshan were all sentenced to death. Zhang Jun, Xu Shengpu, and Wang Xijin were all sentenced to life imprisonment. Zhu Xiaoguan was sentenced to twelve years in prison. Lu Rongtang and Ding Guangzheng were each sentenced to eight years in prison. Wang Hongju and Guo Xishi were each sentenced to six years in prison. One pistol and five bullets were confiscated. After the sentencing, police lawyer Ru Baoyi stated that defendant Lu Rongtang had been sentenced to five years in prison and a fine of 600 yuan by the court on June 2, 1919, for counterfeiting currency. Lu was released on bail of 1,000 yuan pending appeal, but Lu repeatedly failed to appear in court, and the Second Branch Court issued an arrest warrant. Now that he has been apprehended, how should it be handled? Please also make a ruling. Judge Feng then instructed Lu Rongtang to be sent to the Second Branch Court for review.

Charity Lottery Tickets in Greater Demand Than Supply 158

The sales of charity lottery tickets have been reported in previous issues. It is reported that due to the urgent time frame, there was not enough time to print all the tickets. Yesterday, only over 80,000 tickets were issued, and the remaining small portion will be printed in the next few days. As a result, sales outlets continue to request more tickets, but they cannot be fully supplied. There is a situation where demand exceeds supply. In addition to directly purchasing from the Race Club and various sales outlets, some foreigners, such as a member of the Foreign Stock Exchange and a member of the International Savings Society, have also obtained large quantities of lottery tickets from the Finance Bureau and are actively promoting sales. This demonstrates that people from both China and abroad are enthusiastic about supporting charitable causes.

Reader's Advisor

Poor Family and Heavy Burden | Letter from Ms. Zhao Jinglan 164

Sir, I am a woman who married in her teens. At that time, my husband's family consisted of only the two of us, my husband's parents, and one servant. The family has been scholars for generations. Although it is an old-fashioned family, they are very harmonious. My husband is an old man's only son, and his parents naturally love and cherish him and do not want him to attend school. However, he studied in a private school, and it is a pity that he was born late and could not catch up with the imperial examination era for development. Because the family has been scholars for generations, they are unwilling to let him work in the business world. After getting married, he taught Chinese in the local area. Fortunately, in the early years of the Republic of China, the cost of living was not high, and the population was small. The ancestors left a hundred or two acres of land and a little income from teaching, which was enough to make ends meet. However, in the past one or two decades, the situation has changed greatly. I have now given birth to nine children, sons and daughters. The older ones are already studying in high school and junior high school, and the younger ones are studying in elementary school. The youngest is still nursing. Therefore, clothing, food, housing, and education expenses have increased two or three times compared to before. How can we afford it? Prices of everything are gradually increasing, and the family's farmland often suffers from famine. The income from teaching has also decreased compared to before because people are more enlightened and the older students all go to school and are unwilling to study in private schools. Due to these factors, the income has not been enough to cover expenses in the past ten years, and the deficit has gradually increased. Last year, my parents-in-law unfortunately passed away. After all the funeral arrangements were completed, we were heavily in debt and could not afford to pay it back. At this point, after comprehensive consideration, we had no choice but to sell our property to repay the debt. Initially, we thought that after selling the property, we would still have two or three thousand yuan left to start a small business to make a living. However, because of the high grain tax, low land prices, land surveys, and other reasons, people with money are unwilling to buy land. Land prices have plummeted. After selling the property and paying off the debt, we were left with nothing. Now we have no roof over our heads and no place to stand. We still have to eat, wear clothes, live in a house, and go to school. We have no income. My husband earns only a hundred or so yuan from teaching, and I help by doing handicrafts, which is not enough to support the family. Therefore, my husband is actively trying to find a job, but he has no academic background or scientific knowledge. There are many normal school graduates looking forward to becoming elementary school teachers, so there is no room for us to squeeze in. If we go into politics, we have no connections. If we go into business, we are outsiders. Therefore, we have nowhere to turn. As for myself, although I attended elementary school, I did not graduate. Now I am no longer suitable. Handicrafts are my forte, but I do not have the strength to do those rough jobs. I have no knowledge of science and can only recognize a few Chinese characters and calculate a few things. Where can such a person find a job? In short, my husband and I are well-trained in diligence, thrift, honesty, and resourcefulness. In addition, under such difficult circumstances, as long as we do not disgrace our ancestors, maintain our integrity, and protect our children's dignity, we can do any hardship and go any distance. However, even with this firm and enduring aspiration, we still cannot find a job. Sir, what do you think is the best thing to do? Food, clothing, and shelter are indispensable, and education expenses are also essential. My children are very diligent and hardworking. The middle school they attend is the famous Yangzhou Provincial Middle School, and the elementary school they attend is also well-known. Usually, the brothers and sisters study hard together, and none of them fail. Their conduct in school is also good. If we give up education expenses and let them drop out of school, they will give up halfway and cannot become successful. Wouldn't that be heartbreaking? Moreover, even if we save on education expenses, we still have no money for food and clothing. In total, the annual expenses, which cannot be reduced any further, for food, clothing, shelter, and education must be about a thousand yuan, but we have no income and no way to find a job. Isn't it like waiting to die, trapped alive? Sir, you are talented and knowledgeable. I am not afraid of bothering you and have written this long letter detailing my family's situation to ask for your guidance and leadership to lead my family to a bright and happy path to overcome the current difficulties. That would be truly grateful.

Reply: We read your letter in one breath and were truly moved by your plight. The facts are very clear. In your letter, we can clearly see how China's agricultural economy and society are gradually declining. At the same time, it clearly tells us how the general petty bourgeoisie is collapsing rapidly, quickly becoming nakedly poor, and they are still struggling, shouting, looking around blankly, and seeing no way out. This is not the misfortune of Ms. Zhao alone, but indeed a general symptom of the society before us. This is not a simple letter, but a true portrayal of the collapse and decline of the middle class. Since Ms. Zhao's experience is general, and Ms. Zhao asks us to solve this difficulty, the fundamental solution must start from the "general." However, what Ms. Zhao is asking for is a specific solution to the current situation. Regarding this, we can only ask you and your husband to be patient and cope with it for the time being. An annual household expense of about a thousand yuan seems to be able to be reduced a bit. After the eldest son finishes middle school, he does not need to go to college and can find a job. In fact, in this society, studying does not necessarily make you useful. On the other hand, your husband should also think of finding a job. Although it is said that there is a surplus of labor now and it is difficult to find a job, we can only ask your husband to be accommodating and put down the airs of the petty bourgeoisie. As long as you are attentive to some small jobs, you will eventually find one sooner or later. Naturally, this is only a temporary solution. The fundamental cure should start from the root. Only by solving the "whole" can we solve the "part." Ms. Zhao should recognize this, and we hope that your children will also recognize it.

Education News

Important News: Jiangsu Education Funds Released for Half a Month 165

The September Payment Notice Has Been Signed and Can Be Issued Soon. Due to the Provincial Department of Finance's arrears of nearly 3 million yuan in allocations to various counties and provincial subsidies, the provincial education funds have been delayed for years. After representatives from provincial schools and teachers associations went to Nanjing in the middle of this month to continue to petition, the Education Fund Management Office has issued payment notices for the second half of August. After the payment notices were issued, the funds could not be immediately collected in cash due to insufficient funds in the treasury. Director Niu of the Education Fund Management Office, because various schools are in urgent need, in addition to sending section chiefs to various counties to urge for the funds, also borrowed 20,000 yuan from the Wuxi Shanghai Bank and 40,000 yuan from other sources on the 26th to issue the second half of August expenses to the schools. After the funds were raised, various schools can now collect the cash. The September payment notices were signed by the audit committee on the 25th and will be issued after being stamped by the Department of Education and signed by the Director of the Management Office. The payment notice is dated January 10 and is used to withdraw funds from the bank when due. However, it is heard that after the Management Office recently issued the second half of August expenses, the treasury is empty. Section Chief Liu is now urging the borrowing of funds from various counties, and it is heard that Section Chief Yang will also go to various counties soon to urge the funds, hoping to raise 120,000 yuan by January 10 to issue the September expenses to provincial schools and social education institutions.

Senior High School Curriculum Standards (1)

First, Objectives of National Language 171

(1) Enable students to apply the national language and script, deeply understand the inherent culture, and strive to achieve the goal of national revitalization.

(2) In addition to continuing to enable students to freely use vernacular Chinese, cultivate their skills in using classical Chinese to narrate events, reason, express emotions, and convey ideas.

(3) Cultivate students' ability to read and understand ancient books and appreciate famous works of Chinese literature.

(4) Cultivate students' ability to create new language and literature.

Second, Time Allocation 172

Each semester occupies five hours, totaling thirty hours over three academic years. Academic Year Semester Hours Subject Close Reading Extensive Reading Guidance Composition Total Time 1 21 3 1 1 5 2 21 3 1 1 5 3 21 3 1 1 5

Third, Textbook Outline 173

(1) Reading

㈠ Close Reading of Selected Texts: In addition to continuously using the seven standards of junior high school, the arrangement of the sequence, the separation of vernacular and classical Chinese, vernacular Chinese only includes pure literature and texts related to academic thought, classical Chinese focuses on the system in the first academic year, the literary source in the second academic year, and academic thought in the third academic year, each teaching representative works, and may teach literary essentials and application documents.

㈡ Focus Reading of Selected Texts: Based on the principle of (1), increase students' ability to write and read. Determine famous works according to the level of each academic year, about one or two per semester.

㈢ Extensive Reading: Students select and read famous works, either the entire book or selections, individual works scattered in various books, and valuable periodicals, based on their consciousness and interest, guided by the teacher.

(2) Writing Techniques (including grammar, rhetoric, and debate skills, etc., taught within the composition time)

Fourth, Summary of Implementation Methods 174

(1) Reading

㈠ Close Reading of Selected Texts: In the first academic year, the teaching of the system should pay attention to its characteristics and writing methods. In the second academic year, the teaching of representative works of each era should pay attention to its school and evolution. In the third academic year, the teaching of academic thought texts should pay attention to its historical background and influence. (2) Focus Reading of Selected Books: Select the special books for close reading, briefly explain its historical status, literary value, author's era background, and personal style, etc., collectively or individually, and instruct reading methods, points, time, and reference books, and cultivate students' ability to use reference books and reference materials at any time.

㈢ Extensive Reading Method: Same as focus reading of selected books.

㈣ Examination Method: Examine students' reading progress at any time, such as reviewing notes, temporary tests, or asking them to report and discuss in turn.

(2) Composition

㈠ Writing Techniques

1. Grammar should continue to pay attention to the similarities and differences between vernacular and classical Chinese. The special features of grammar in ancient books should also be explained separately to help students understand ancient books.

2. Rhetoric should focus on the organization and system of articles, the method of diction, and the types of rhetoric. Attention should also be paid to the appreciation of literary works and the discrimination of writers' styles to cultivate talent and the ability to appreciate famous works of Chinese literature.

3. Debate Skills: Attention should be paid to the methods of debate, the collection of evidence, the correctness of judgment, and the rebuttal of opponents to cultivate students' clear minds.

㈡ Composition Exercises

1. Assigned Composition

(A) In-class Composition: Cultivate students' habit and ability to write quickly.

(B) Out-of-class Composition: Cultivate students' ability to think meticulously and exert themselves as much as possible in writing.

2. Translation: In order to train students' accuracy in writing techniques, attention should be paid to translation. For example: (A) Translate classical Chinese into vernacular Chinese, (B) Translate vernacular Chinese into classical Chinese, (C) Translate ancient rhyming texts into vernacular prose, (D) Translate foreign short articles into Chinese classical or vernacular literature.

3. Reading Notes: Ask students to write systematic or fragmented notes on their reading experiences or questions to cultivate their diligent and cautious habits.

4. Records of Tours and Visits: Encourage students to observe, collect materials, judge, and describe.

5. Special Research: Propose research topics, and students collect data and special records.

A Respectful Appeal to College and University Students Nationwide to Implement Education to Save the Nation (You Huai Gao) 175

(9) The only way to save the nation is "Educational Service." I do not hope that college and university students across the country will immediately go to the countryside to implement it, but I hope that within three months, in major events and secondary schools across the country, united people can quickly establish the National Education Salvation Association. After the organization is complete, then unite the educational salvation associations in various places to form the National Education Salvation Association to ask the government to issue an order, with the following intentions:

"All college and university students nationwide must, after graduation, abide by the National Education Salvation Association's charter and, under the guidance of the National Education Salvation Association, go to various villages to perform educational service for one year. College and university students who have not performed educational service for more than one year will ㈠ not be given a diploma, ㈡ not be allowed to take up employment, ㈢ not be allowed to marry, ㈣ not be allowed to inherit property."

Students who are unwilling to provide education to others during this time of national crisis are showing that they cannot fulfill their duties and lack empathy. Therefore, they are considered to be people without civic virtue and should be abandoned by the people. However, after students have completed their educational service, the government should hold a grand adult ceremony every year. The Chairman of the Chinese Government and the Chairmen of each province should personally award educational service certificates to confirm that they are a supreme honor for the people.

Since students have fulfilled their responsibility of contributing their talents, the bourgeoisie must also fulfill their responsibility of contributing their wealth. Then, the government should issue an order, with the following main points:

"All citizens of the Republic of China who enjoy property rights should collect a few percent of the national tax as an education salvation tax to fund the national education salvation. The economic management association should be organized by each province or county to be responsible for the custody and distribution of funds. The charter will be formulated by the National Education Salvation Association. If any citizen can automatically donate education salvation funds, the government should reward them according to their merits."

Currently, there are people who can provide education and there are funds, but to educate 300 million people and spread it across 4 million square kilometers of land is an unprecedented event in Chinese history. Therefore, it is necessary to gather specialized talents from across the country in the capital and various provincial and municipal areas to organize the National Education Salvation Association to design, guide, and operate this great undertaking of education to save the nation. The government should then issue an order, with the following main points:

"All higher specialized talents among the citizens of the Republic of China should gather within one month in the capital or the metropolises of various provincial and municipal areas to organize the National Education Salvation Association and its various provincial and municipal branches to design, guide, and promote rural education affairs across the country, and organize various statistical bureaus for national social people's livelihood resources, and can freely use the Central Radio Station to broadcast nationwide. All expenses will be provided by the government, but members are all honorary positions."

Six. Applied documents. All declarations, contracts, regulations, advertisements, and other official documents can be made by students.

Seven. Literary works. All novels, poems, plays, and dramas can be made by students.

Lin Zhuguang Appointed Principal of Quanzhang Middle School 179

The Student Unrest Ends Temporarily

The Guomin News Agency, Quanzhang Middle School in this city, previously had student unrest due to improper measures by the school authorities, which were instigated by a small number of people. It has been fully resolved after mediation by the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Education Bureau. It is reported that the school board has appointed Lin Zhuguang as the principal and expelled a large number of students, dissolved the school protection group, reading club, drama club, etc. As for the school's student self-government association, it has no extracurricular activities and has been filed with the Municipal Party Department, so it is still allowed to exist. Free Talk

Fragments of Memory 195

— Shi

Life is like a stream of flowing water, often stirring up waves. My life is short, but there are still some things that often make me painfully recall.

When I was just able to remember, I often heard my great-grandmother say while I sat on her lap: "You will definitely be a good child in the future. On the night you were born, your grandfather dreamed of the largest tree in the countryside catching fire, and your mother dreamed of a rural teacher coming to her house and refusing to leave. When they woke up from their dreams, you were crying in the world."

It seems strange, but I was already a teacher in my twenty-second year.

But with my birth, unfortunate things continued to happen.

One of my aunts repeatedly told me:

"When you grow up in the future, you should repay me well. Without me, you wouldn't be alive now. Your mother liked to gamble the most, often gambling until dawn, and your father often didn't come home at night. When you woke up late at night, you would cry. Your temper was bad since you were a child, and your crying was so urgent. When your mother heard your crying, she put down her cards and returned to her own room, starting to hold you and coax you to sleep. But she could rarely trick you. As soon as she put you down, you would cry loudly again. Your mother was thinking about cards, but she couldn't put you down, so she got angry and threw you on the ground. Several times, when I ran to your mother's room to see, you were already lying on the ground, cold, and had been dead for a long time."

But the most unfortunate thing is that I completely inherited my mother's irritable personality.

Since the day I entered elementary school, I was expelled from school two or three times every year, and it was always because of quarrels with classmates. The students in the same class had to be subject to my control. If they refused to obey me, I would overcome them with force. After school at three or four o'clock in the afternoon, it was time for me to use force: leading a group of classmates under my command, lying in ambush at the crossroads, waiting for the rebel, catching him and beating him until he knelt on the ground begging for mercy before letting him go. In the end, the students in the same school were no longer in my eyes, and I moved the target to the neighboring elementary school. I can't describe the situation of that kind of fighting with my pen, but whenever I think of that time, I immediately think of the scene of the two clans killing each other in Romeo and Juliet. The most regrettable thing is that neither side had weapons. Such a rebellious elementary school student entered the strictest middle school.

Expulsion was still a common thing, but not because of quarrels with classmates, but because it was related to the teachers. I still clearly remember our middle school's thin-faced, bald-headed, round-nosed, rat-eyed dean of discipline. He didn't talk about justice much, and always favored the teachers. Whenever I was summoned to the discipline office from the classroom, when he showed his power, I would reason with him. If he didn't reason with me, I would no longer reason with him, and let him do whatever he wanted. His punishment was always severe, but I had classmates as my backing, and I would ask the school authorities in the name of the whole class, because each incident was not entirely about me personally, but was often instigated by many classmates.

Times have changed. Those unreasonable teachers and deans may have been replaced by new enlightened people. Until now, I still feel that none of the conflicts I had with the teachers in middle school should be blamed on me.

Between my time from elementary school to middle school and leaving middle school, our family encountered several storms.

My father was in the banking industry, specializing in buying and selling stocks. He was very lucky at first and created a small bourgeois family. But in the year I graduated from elementary school, my father's speculation failed, and our family encountered bankruptcy for the first time.

On Food, Sex, and Desire 196

— Yu Dafu

"Food and sex are human nature." This is absolutely true. "Behind the red gates, meat and wine rot, while the fields are full of skeletons of the starved dead," so there must be class struggle. On one side, "The harem beauties number three thousand," "Each day the monarch cannot see enough," while on the other, "In Stone Moat Village, husband and wife bid farewell," "Husband guards the Xiao Pass, while his wife is in Wu," so there must be revolution. However, the desires for food and sex, because they are basic desires, are very easy to satisfy. No matter how great an epicure you are, as long as you have a jug of wine, a chicken, three bowls of white rice, and a big pancake, you can always be defeated. After eating your fill, even if He Zeng invites you as a guest, you can no longer eat it. As for sex, I think no matter how energetic you are, ten women at most will be enough to deal with. After experiencing ten women, even Xi Shi and Tai Zhen can no longer arouse sexual desire. Therefore, primitive basic desires are easy to fulfill; the most difficult thing to deal with is that abstract desire that goes beyond what is necessary, endlessly, and even becomes a morbid obsession. Philosophers call it desire, and the desire mentioned in the old Chinese essays is this thing.

According to Western philosophers, this desire is the driving force of evolution. Because of desire, everyone goes to work, invent, save... and then there is society, evolution, civilization... This is also true, of course, from the good aspects of desire. But in China, the good aspects of this desire are not developed, and what is making great progress is precisely the bad aspects of things that are spurred by this desire. Because of desire, Chinese people want to scrape the land, sell official titles, compete for territory... ×××, in the end, they forget the purpose completely, and even recognize the means as the end. The miser in The Scholars, who refused to breathe his last when he was dying, only begrudging the two wicks in the oil lamp, is not an imagination, but a common thing in Chinese society. Precisely because of this, Lao Tzu wants to persuade people to be content, Buddhists want to talk bitterly about Nirvana, Schopenhauer wants to extinguish will, and Russell says that all useless desires should be suppressed, and the creation of desires must be increased, which is the fundamental law to eliminate war. The teachings of the wise are indeed correct, but unfortunately China has evolved too early.

Before the European Industrial Revolution, China, thousands of years ago, was full of these great teachings of contentment and inaction, so in an era when the growth of desire should be encouraged and the progress of material things should be promoted, China fell into a state of ease and freedom. By the nineteenth century, when the splendor and wealth of Western material civilization flowed into China, the Chinese, who had long suffered from the dryness and loneliness of inaction and contentment, jumped from one extreme to the other. As a result, the situation is getting worse and worse, and the floods are raging. We Chinese have become a nation that lets them (Westerners) create, and we will enjoy it. While Spengler is worrying about the year of the decline of Western culture, Chinese dignitaries happen to be wearing silk socks costing forty taels of silver a pair and opening bottles of champagne costing fifty taels of silver a bottle. With a thunderous sound, the armies of Japan and other imperialists marched into China majestically. The poor old people not only had no food and sex, but could not even keep their lives. Patriotic people began to discuss the reasons why they were strong and we were weak. So the conservatives said that material civilization harmed China, and the progressives said that the pioneers, the sages and wise men were the culprits who caused the weakness of modern China. Both sides have their reasons, but it seems that neither side has said it all correctly.

In short, the first is the question of 'timing': China became too backward because it evolved too early, and in the era when material civilization should have been promoted, only ghost-like spiritual civilization was promoted. The second is the question of 'selection': Western material civilization eroded the East at the same time, but Japan took the good aspects of it, while China only took the bad aspects of it. For example, if it is a walnut, the Japanese take its meat, while the Chinese only take its shell.

What is the crime of material civilization? What is the crime of desire?

George Bernard Shaw and the Actress's Love Affair 197

— Zhao Jingshen

Recently, there is a collection of letters, Ellen Terry and Bernard Shaw, published, with more than 400 pages, recording the love letters between these two people. Terry was a famous actress. At the time of the correspondence, she was already fifty years old, but she was still Ellen Terry, and many people admired her. George Bernard Shaw praised her art: "Dear Ellen, undoubtedly, you must be deified before you can perform in a drama. Once you enter the realm of deification, you will fear nothing."

Shaw boasted that he was a descendant of Irish nobles. He was eight years younger than Ellen.

Their love affair was somewhat different. Ellen was a woman without great ambitions. She was just an actress who reached the peak of her career. Because her nature was close to that of an actress, her fame was accidental, not "achieved by force." George Bernard Shaw, however, was a man with great ambitions. He wrote dramas not only for the sake of drama, but for everything he did was purposeful. In his love letters, he still did not forget his great career, so the lover George Bernard Shaw was entangled with the playwright George Bernard Shaw. He himself once said in a love letter to Ellen: "I love women, but I also sincerely like other things. Most women take a man and a lifetime as the whole world; but I need to have relations with ancient and modern times, both at home and abroad. I want to make the writing machine accelerate. Love is just my entertainment and rest."

When this letter began, Shaw was writing theater reviews for the Saturday Review. Terry was the protagonist of the Lyceum Theatre.

This letter is not a letter from a monk and a nun. Of course, it will not be very disciplined, but it was not until the end of this book that they had a taste of flesh! Sincere and strong. Ellen besieged him. He had to write to her several times a day and write very long letters. Shaw also besieged Ellen. Ellen wrote him just as many letters, but not as long as his. Shaw wrote beautifully and romantically. Even on the train, which was shaking very badly, he was still fascinated by the "beautiful countryside and ghostly moonlight" and wrote many affectionate words. One night he went to Dorking and wrote to Ellen: "I am now very attached to you. I am restless. A man's restlessness is always for a woman, and my restlessness is for Terry."

I don't know if it was for revenge or for other reasons, Shaw married Charlotte Frances Payne Townshend in 1898. He wrote to Ellen calling Payne a "woman with light green eyes and millions of dollars." He also said that his love with her was just to change to something fresh. Later, he said that he "likes her very much, but loving her is too much." Ellen also scolded Payne in her letters. These letters have been destroyed by Ellen, so there is a part missing from this collection of letters. After the marriage, Shaw was still as affectionate to Ellen as before, but Ellen had greatly changed her attitude.

Until 1925, they continued to correspond, but the fire of passion had long been extinguished, and the flames had long been dimmed.

A Proposal 198

— Yang

I would now like to make a proposal in front of the people of the whole country, namely: "Change the Yue Wu Mu Temple on the West Lake to "Qin Hui Temple", pull down the statues of Yue Fei and his son, and replace them with bronze statues of Qin Hui and his wife. Mouye Mouye, and Mr. Hu Shi, etc. are entitled to be enshrined in the two wings. Qin Hui and his wife have their original positions. (The gate of Yue Temple) Replace the iron statues of Yue Fei and his son." The reasons are as follows:

㈠ During the Song Dynasty, Yue Fei advocated war, and Qin Hui advocated peace. Now it is Yue Fei who advocates peace, and Qin Hui who advocates war. Since the facts have been reversed, the way of rewarding good and punishing evil must also be changed. The praise and derogation in the Spring and Autumn Annals is almost more glorious than the Huakun and more fearsome than the axe.

㈡ Mr. Hu Shi recently discovered (according to what he told his friends) that according to the Song History, the environment in which the Song Dynasty was located had to surrender to the Jin and had to negotiate peace. Qin Hui's advocacy of peace was actually a mature plan for the country, with a unique service. His execution of Yue Fei also had the bitter intention of pacifying the internal and external troubles.

A song is used to publicize this matter. The song says:

Yue Fei was originally a bastard:

He deserved to be beheaded, his family confiscated, and disaster extended to his relatives;

Qin Hui was originally a hero:

Of course, he killed people, set fires, betrayed the country, sought peace, and enjoyed wealth and honor like Mount Tai!

"Bastard" and "hero" each accept,

Who cares about the worship and resentment of future generations!

Now people's hearts have changed greatly,

Yue Fei has experience

Qin Hui is not,

The former advocated peace,

The latter advocated war,

The fate of leaving a bad or good name also turns,

Each has a thousand years!

Impressions of Suzhou (4) 199

— Fu Zhen

Under the guidance of Pai, I took the small motorboat from Suzhou to Bentuo, advancing in the waves full of rural scenery. After more than two hours, I arrived at Bentuo. Bentuo is a small town near Suzhou City, with a very dense population. It is about six or seven miles from Bentuo to Tianping, passing Lingyan Mountain, you can reach Tianping Mountain directly. From Lingyan to Tianping Mountain, there are very wide imperial roads built, paved with bricks. According to Yuan, it was built by Emperor Qianlong when he went to the south of the Yangtze River, but hasn't it been buried in weeds until now?

When we were advancing on the imperial road buried in weeds, only the branches of the trees on both sides of the mountain were playing natural music to accompany our lonely companions; the sound of dry grass rustling under our feet also naturally echoed the singing of the branches, breaking the silence for a moment. 丨丨 No, it can also be said that it made the heart feel the silence of this mountain and field, so silent that there were only the rustling footsteps and the sound of the wind in the branches. The scenery of "a cicada chirping makes the forest more quiet, and a bird singing makes the mountain more secluded" in the poems of the ancients is only now being realized.

When we were walking on the imperial road, we also touched the reeds on both sides, which covered the earth as white as snow, and swayed east and west with the wind like willow catkins. Their light and graceful posture was like palace fairies wearing snow-white feather clothes, dancing in neon clothes. They were nodding to us, welcoming our arrival, they danced and danced with the wind, whether it was in the morning when the sun rose wearing colorful clothes, or in the evening when the sunset glow was dimming, they were always dancing. They appreciated themselves, didn't seek to be known, didn't like people's praise, and didn't care about people's ridicule; they always danced, they could really show a mocking smile to humans. But, no, they still warmly welcome us. When Chang'e hangs up her silver lantern, I think it must be the time when they are most proud. They are really for art, they are really respectable companions on our journey.

In a surprised gaze, I discovered very unusual strange rocks, standing on the mountain one by one. That is what Yuan told me about Tianping Mountain. Outside the Hongfo Temple at the foot of the mountain, there were many maple trees standing. They stood very tall, stubbornly maintaining their old spirit. Some of the leaves were still green like spring; but the green of spring was not their era, their era was coming; some of the leaves that got the weather first had gradually turned yellow, gradually turned red.

We walked up the mountain from the Buddhist temple, and there were many stone inscriptions on both sides, hurrying up the mountain, there was no time to look closely. A monk in the temple warmly greeted us, and many paintings and calligraphy were hung in the reception room. Next to the reception room, there is a bowl of Meng Spring, which uses a large tank to store water. The water is spring water, which is connected by a bamboo pole. The source of the water is very thin, flowing slowly. How clear and transparent it is, it is very pure, like transparent crystal; when the spring water falls into the tank, it is like crystal pearls merging together.

Long Creative Writing

The Crossroads of Era and Love 30 200

— Zhang Ziping

Although the four glass-paneled folding doors to the main room were tightly shut, the bright electric light inside reflected everything on the surface clearly. Three young women were gathered around a square table, applying makeup. The one sitting directly across from Haiquan's line of sight was the clearest. Her face was covered in white powder, with extra red rouge on her cheeks. She was leaning forward, looking at a small mirror on the table, shaping her eyebrows as she drew them, talking all the while. He could only see her lips moving constantly but could not hear her voice. Haiquan looked at their bodies again; they were all wearing white velvet shirts, exposing a portion of their snow-white necks and chests. The pair of high peaks on their chests were also quite prominent. The other two, one with her back to Haiquan and one sitting sideways, were less clearly visible.

"How could daughters from ordinary families dress up like little actresses on a stage with all that rouge and powder?"

The scene inside stunned Haiquan. He was a little surprised and wondered if he had found the wrong house number. So, he looked up at the address above and saw clearly that it was number fifteen.

"This is clearly the home of women engaged in immoral professions. University student Zhuo Shuhua would never live in a place like this."

But then he thought of the previous criticisms that some university girls were high-class prostitutes. Could the lively Ms. Zhuo be this kind of woman?

He pondered for a moment, not daring to knock, but not wanting to leave either. Fortunately, a gust of cold wind carried the stench from the garbage bin to his nose, and he woke up as if from a dream, taking two or three steps toward the alley entrance.

"Ms. Zhuo is definitely not this kind of woman. I can assert that! ......"

He walked and thought, and later, as if an astronomer had discovered a special comet, a smile spread across his face. At the same time, he clenched his left fist tightly, striking a pose as if giving a speech.

"...Why? If she were such a frivolous woman, she would never have so frankly invited me to this place."

He thought for a moment. Then, he turned back again, returning to the door of number fifteen, made up his mind, and knocked on the door knocker.

"Who is it?"

As soon as he knocked, he heard someone inside asking.

Haiquan put his eyes to the crack in the door again, looking inside. One of the three women had already opened the screen door and was standing in the doorway of the main room.

"Is there someone named Zhuo living here?"

"Yes. Go around to the back door."

Haiquan was about to turn around when he suddenly heard someone calling him from above.

"Mr. Lin? I'm sorry, please go to the back door. ......"

This was exactly the voice he had been waiting for. He hurriedly looked up and saw Zhuo Shuhua sticking half her body out of the upstairs window, smiling and waving at him. Her lively manner was no different from in school. Haiquan was so happy to see her that he couldn't even speak. He just,

New Record for Margin Trading: Production Especially Abundant, Slashed Today, Broken Tomorrow 201

Large Closing, Chinese | Silver Dollar Transactions Busy 204

| Year-End Interest Rates Are Seen As Fixed |

The Silver and Money Industry's Procedures Have Been Tedious In Recent Days. Transactions Have Been More Frequent. The Human Resources Department Is All Busy Ensuring the Year-End Closing. This Year, Because Commerce Is Sluggish, Not Much Has Been Loaned. This Is Enough to Meet the Year-End Closing. New Accounts Are Easier to Handle Than Last Year. However, Old Debts Are Frightening After Clearing Up. I Fear It Will Not Be Easy to Deal With. As for the Interest Rates, There Is No Grand Situation to Speak of During This Year-End Closing. However, Yesterday's Silver Dollar Transactions Were Still Not Weak. Probably Just Internal Buying and Selling Within the Industry.

The Silver Dollar's Rise and Fall Are Limited, and the Silver Interest Rate Is Still Opened at Two Fen. When the "Silver Dollar" Market Opened in the Morning, People's Hearts Were Dispersed. Although Banks Had an Appetite to Buy, There Was a Lack of Competition. Therefore, the Interest Rate Was Always Sluggish. The Closing Was at Seven Jiao One Fen Three Li Three Hao Seven Hu Ban, Slightly Smaller Than the Previous Day by One Hao Two Hu Ban. The Afternoon Market Then Turned Higher by Two Hao Ban, to Seven Jiao One Fen Three Li Six Hao Two Hu Ban. As a Result, It Was Better Than the Previous Afternoon by One Hao Two Hu Ban. The "Silver Interest Rate" in Both the Morning and Afternoon Markets Was Still Two Fen, Roughly the Same As the Previous Day. The Initial Interest Rate Was Still No More Than Two or Three Fen. The Silver Root Situation Was Stable and Loose As Before.

Jiangnan Drops and Rises Suddenly. Copper Coins Seem to Be Released Long-Term Again. Transactions Were Done for Over 38,000 Strings of Wen. Silver Remittances and Settlements Are Trivial. The New York Stock Market Shows Slight Firmness 206

New Feng Foreign Firm Report (28th) Wednesday New York Stock Market Was Slightly Firmer. After the Opening, It Gradually Rose Step By Step. Some People Threw Out Input Sect, To Low Prices, and To Offset Tax Losses, So It Immediately Returned. General Motors and North American Airlines Were Especially Thrown Out at First. The Later Market Widely Spread That the Railway Industry Had a Significant Step Up in November, and Industry Conditions Were Better Than The Prediction. Therefore, the General Trend Became Tight Again. According to Gangtie Century Report, This Week's Steel Workload Is 13 Percent. Although It Is Due to the End of the Year and Christmas Holidays, It Is Still Higher Than the New Low Price Since the Depression. The Price Department Is Expected to Gradually Improve After the New Year. The Number of Transactions Today Totals 1.6 Million Shares. The Dow Jones Index Is Listed on the Left.

The Cotton Market Has a Stable Trend 208

The Cotton Market Is Firm, and the Trend Is Flat. Because a Certain Manufacturer Has Short Positions in Recent Months, There Is No Intention to Offset Them, and the Xihe Coarse Cotton Purchased in Tianjin Is Withdrawn in January , Because of This, People's Hearts Are Restrained, and Some Profit-Taking Bulls Take Advantage of the Rise to Settle. However, the Current American Situation Is Stable, Prices Are Rising Daily, and There Are Concerns That Exchange Rates Will Be Soft. The Market Is Still Difficult to Go Down. Therefore, General Buyers Tighten the Distant Months and Never Let Go.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Conversations

On Being an Official 226

— Wu

Regarding being an official, I believe it is indeed a very important matter, and it is worth discussing.

Before our fathers had even added a copper top to their red-tasseled hats, they would dream day and night: Oh! From a student, to a scholar, from a scholar, to a licentiate, from a licentiate to a Jinshi, and then begin to be an official. If one wanted to be an honest official, one might as well be poor and be a small official in the capital. If one wanted to make a fortune, one would have to find a teacher and seek an outside post… Finally, of course, fire-branded servants would stand before the door, the stone lions would be flanked by tall flagpoles, and the ancestral hall would be filled with plaques from one's own family. How imposing, how magnificent! The ancestors' thick virtues would of course be fully realized, and there would even be the good fortune of cultivating oneself into an immortal. As for those who lacked virtue, alas…it goes without saying, even mentioning it would be heartbreaking.

Since this is the case, these fathers are our fathers, then accepting the teachings of our fathers is of course the duty of us sons. Thus, we must go from elementary school, to middle school, … to university, to studying abroad. But something seems a bit off. After studying abroad, can one necessarily become an official? That's a bit hard to say, so this road may not be passable. Therefore, if we follow our fathers' old ways, we will inevitably be fools.

So, what should we do? Of course, there is a reason.

Needless to say, everyone is a sensible person. To be an official, one does not necessarily need qualifications, and even less does one need worthless knowledge. Money goes without saying, but the most important thing is to be good at bragging. If you insist that you are a doctor, who will really check your diploma?

Then, after becoming an official, what should one do? This is even more worthy of study. At first, you must learn to wear a Zhongshan suit and carry a leather briefcase, and the briefcase must be filled to the brim. More importantly, you must be familiar with the Premier's will and practice three minutes of silence. When you are still a small official, you must endure your temper and be absolutely obedient. When the section chief scolds you for being a fool in official language, you must quickly respond with "Yes, yes, yes." If you are rewarded with a slap in the face, it is even more of a compliment. Then you must touch your burning face and say, "I dare not, I dare not!" As for being a high official, it is of course very different. Walking into the office, you might as well slam the table and shout, "Why hasn't it been done yet? The country is paying you, what are you doing!" But what exactly hasn't been done well? You don't have to worry about it, as long as the subordinates are submissive.

As for what benefits there are to being an official, even a rough villager who touches a cow's behind would know. Making a fortune goes without saying, and even marrying twenty concubines would not be considered bigamy by law. Generally speaking, a small official may not easily collude with foreign countries, but a high official can openly betray the country without any problem. If you are a military officer, the most taboo thing is to dare to confront imperialism. Domestic civil wars, on the other hand, can be fought several times. Occupying a territory is like occupying a treasure trove. Forcibly planting opium is an excellent method. Looking back at history, you can find many precedents. It is better to be infamous for ten thousand years than to be fragrant for a thousand years.

It's a long story, so I have to stop halfway. If there is a chance, I will explain it next time. Besides, Chinese scholars have always been well-versed in the way of being an official, so why should I, a junior, waste my breath?

The Confusion of Modern Women 227

— Chen Ruizhen

Common Sense

Moisture-Proofing Matches 228

— Xi Nong

We know that the method of preventing wood from getting damp is to coat it with a layer of paint. Similarly, this similar method can be applied to moisture-proofing matches. Crush a small amount of rosin and place it in alcohol, heat it to dissolve it, and then immerse the match heads in the solution. After a few minutes, take it out and let it dry. In this way, even if the matches are accidentally dropped into the water, they can still be lit.

Oiling Machine Belts

Applying a type of oil to the belts that rotate on machines can significantly increase the turning efficiency, and the belts will also last longer. This type of oil is made by cooking two parts of lead yellow with four or five parts of sesame oil in two parts of water until it becomes a gel. When using, mix it with an appropriate amount of turpentine.

Removing Old Paint Stains

A simple method for removing old paint stains from cotton fabrics is to mix one part of turpentine with two parts of ammonia solution, shake it vigorously to make it emulsify, and then use cotton wool or a brush to apply it to the old paint stains. After a few minutes, wait for the paint stains to soften, and then wipe it off with cotton.

A Homemade Glue

Sometimes we often have such a need to glue paper and leather together. If we use ordinary paste or glue to glue them, it is often not easy to stick, or even if it sticks, many wrinkles will be produced, which will easily come off. Therefore, it is best to make a kind of glue yourself that meets this need, that is, dissolve 200 parts of gum arabic and 1 part of tannic acid each in water, and then mix it with 50 parts of glycerin and 10 parts of glucose. One thing to pay attention to here is that the less water used when dissolving tannic acid, the better.

Writing on Glass

The easiest way to engrave something on glass is to simply use a steel pen dipped in silicic acid to write. However, the strokes engraved in this way are very thick. If you want to engrave very fine things, you must apply the following method!

Place one and a half liters of water in each of two glass bottles and dissolve 18 grams of hydrofluoric acid and grams of sulfide. Also, place half a liter of water in the other bottle and dissolve 7 grams of zinc dichloride in it. After it is completely dissolved, add 30 grams of concentrated hydrochloric acid.

When using, mix equal amounts of the solutions in the two bottles and write on the glass with a steel pen. To make it clear when writing, you can add a few drops of ink to make it appear in detail.

Sister, What Kind of Thing is "Saving the Country"? 229

— Yi Ping

I never thought that I would meet you, who had been missing for five years, in such a gathering. When you receive this letter, don't be surprised, because I am not used to sitting for a long time in this annoying jazz music. Thank you for telling me the address, so I will write here about my situation after we parted, which you were eager to know last night.

Five years ago, in my hometown, I was undeniably regarded as a dissolute child. You are a descendant of a scholarly family and the daughter of a noble family. After regarding my unwarranted sins as facts, you no longer met with me. So I was expelled from my hometown. For five years, I have been racking my brains and working my body, exchanging sweat and blood for three meals a day. Looking back, among my many fellow villagers, if you say I am a dissolute child, I really can't find a reason, because I have tasted too much bitterness, so I have also met many kinds of people. A few days before the New World held this great and grand National Salvation Entertainment Conference, I was forced by a friend to buy a few tickets. Of course, since the September 18th Incident, from the Northeast Volunteer Army fighting bloody battles against the Japanese to today, every citizen who cannot go to the front line should do their best to fulfill their national responsibility. So, no matter how poor my purse was that day, I generously bought them. Last night, without asking Little Confused whether it was an auspicious day, I made an appointment with a few friends to go to the New World during a week of work. With my head held high, I followed the crowd into the New World. I knew it wasn't like coming in to play for two cents as usual. Stepping into the dance hall was naturally not accidental, but I, a dissolute child, made an exception for the first time. Who would have thought I would meet my sister, who had been missing for five years? I felt that I had lost more than I gained by being branded as a "dissolute child."

Sister, you are the daughter of a noble family, how can you be involved in a group of dancers, so that you can't tell your worth? A white face, red lips, piled with messy black hair, matched with a body trembling in a narrow cheongsam, everything, if you don't mind, I'm afraid you will also be covered with the suspicion of a "dissolute girl." However, in these chaotic years, even if the country is about to be destroyed, it can be put aside (please forgive me for saying such cold-blooded words). I still have to earn three meals of bitter tea and light meals every day. It's really going to be regarded as a "dissolute child" if I tell you these irrelevant words.

However, after exchanging a few words with your Mr. Li last night, I know that you are doing your best to help this National Salvation Entertainment Conference. I said in the tone of an old man, "Please start from the root." As for me, I haven't made a fortune in five years and can't wear the "dancing to save the country" suit like your Mr. Li, but I am still well-behaved and still retain the true colors of a "dissolute child" five years ago. I don't dare to boast in front of others after spending two or three yuan on such a major event as "saving the country." Sister, if you are willing to give me some advice, please tell me, what kind of thing is "saving the country"?

The final statement is that I didn't have the intention of "dancing to save the country" when I stepped into the dance hall last night.

After Unemployment 230

— Wang Ying

I have been unemployed since last month. God! I am not a bourgeois capitalist, so the panic and pain of life are needless to say. The most embarrassing thing for me is the sarcasm of the people around me. It's no wonder they want to insult me, because I am already a so-called unemployed vagrant!

Fang! Wife! She is very understanding. Although she suffers with me, she has no complaints, unlike the love of so-called modern women, which is completely based on money. But I, this useless husband, just feel ashamed. There is also my white-haired old father, who still cannot be fed and clothed. Alas! I, this unfilial son!

Yesterday I took my son, Xiong'er, for a stroll on the street. In fact, my heart was surging with thoughts, so I had no leisure to stroll.

Xiong'er really asked me with a surprised look:

"Daddy! Yesterday, Ming'er! His little friend! Insulted me for being a poor ghost. I thought it was true. Why do other people eat fat fish and big meat and live in high-rise buildings? Why are we so miserable?"

My fragile heartstrings were violently stimulated, and two lines of hot tears involuntarily burst out due to emotional impulses.

"Daddy! You were talking and laughing just now. Why are you crying now? I can't agree with you! Daddy! Did I say something wrong? Daddy, don't cry anymore." Xiong'er raised his small hand in horror and wiped away my crystal tears.

"No! Child!" I stroked her short hair and said softly to him, "Don't you want to eat fat fish and big meat? Child! Blame our bad fate. We are people who have been forgotten by happiness!" He seemed to understand what I meant and nodded slowly.

On the way back, I thought that since I lost my job, the more valuable clothes have been pawned at Changsheng Pawnshop. The autumn wind has risen and there are no warm clothes. No! I don't even have money for tomorrow's meal. The accumulated rent, debts, and everything will be pressing down on me. "Alas! What is really good?" I, a weak person, uttered a cry of sorrow.

Alas! God, how cruel you are to people. God of happiness, you have long forgotten me!……Poor people can only……!

Clerk Correspondence 231

Reading, Entertainment, and Sports Combined Editor:

After reading the three organizations in your column, I have some thoughts! Because these "Weekly Academic Discussion Meeting," "Amateur Peking Opera Research Society," and "Amateur National Martial Arts Group" are all very narrowly defined. I think it is better to expand a little and have a whole organization rather than one organization in the east and one in the west. It is more systematic and more effective. So my idea is to combine all the clerks and apprentices and organize a "Business Youth Life Mutual Aid Society" to summarize all the above small organizations in one place. Wouldn't it be more beneficial to the interests of our clerks and apprentices? However, such an organization cannot be successful with just a few people. I would like to provide our clerks and apprentices with a chance to study and research.

I have had this idea for many years, but because of the environment, I have never been determined to do it, and my personal ability is limited. Moreover, I have now left the business world. Although I used to be an apprentice, a clerk, and then a store owner, it is all in the past.

I now hope that our staff and apprentices should automatically organize themselves to seek their own life development and solve the problems of physical, moral, intellectual, group, and all other aspects.

This is my little opinion, offered to the clerks and apprentices for everyone to study and research.

Li Ermo on December 23rd evening

Editor:

After reading the "Organization of Three Groups" in your column, I have an opinion to offer.

(1) Mr. Zhang uses his spare time on Sundays to exchange knowledge with each other; (2) Mr. Ma and Mr. Chen use their spare time for proper entertainment; (3) Mr. Zhou advocates the inherent Chinese martial arts to temper everyone's physique. I think all three are right and there is a need for connection.

Because knowledge is something that everyone needs and is endless; at the same time, in order to increase the efficiency of doing things, one must have a strong physique; to avoid the boredom and dullness of life, one must rely on proper entertainment to regulate. Since these three are all needed in life, why not expand the organization and connect with each other? What do you gentlemen think?

Meng Yin, December 24th

Editor:

I have silently observed the psychology of most people in society and found that they always have some differences: because of the differences in psychology, their views and interests in things are also different.

For example, most people who focus on literature do not like sports, resulting in a weak body that easily gets sick. If it is incurable, wouldn't it be a great pity? Or those who are proficient in national martial arts, whose strength is enough to lift a tripod, but who are "illiterate" and "unable to solve difficult problems," will undoubtedly be despised by society. As for entertainment, as long as it is proper, it is also an enjoyment that should be had in the course of life.

Therefore, in my humble opinion, in order to develop scholarship and physique at the same time, and then use proper entertainment to regulate life, we must combine reading, entertainment, and sports into one. Moreover, we can connect everyone's feelings and regulate different mentalities: by this, we can also consolidate the common front of our youth and concentrate the fighting power of our youth. Ask Mr. Ma and Mr. Zhou and the readers of Shangming, is it right or wrong?

Zhang Siwei, December 24th.

Editor's note: The above three letters actually want the three individual groups to unite into one large group by appointment. The intention is very good.

However, we also offered a little opinion in the "Organization of Three Groups", that is, (1) be cautious before organizing; (2) be persistent after organizing; (3) do not have thoughts of rights, and be able to take responsibility.

Dear readers: We feel that the social problems are serious and cannot be solved by a few people. If you really want to find a solution, you must rely on the power of the masses. So we are also willing to support from the side and see you achieve it as soon as possible.

But this is everyone's business. Before many readers express their opinions, we will of course not express any opinions.
