Novel

Sympathizers (Continued 9) 233

— Zhang Henshui

He picked up the dry tobacco pipe on the table and looked at it, turning it around with both hands for a few times. He lowered his head and wondered what he should say to justify himself. Sister-in-law Wang had been paying attention to him for a long time, thinking that he wanted to smoke the dry tobacco, so she reached into her pocket, groped for a while, and took out six or seven red-headed matches, all of which were placed on the table, and smiled: You smoke. Meng Guobao smiled: Country people are really thrifty. A few foreign matches are like treasures. Probably the electricity used by city people for one night is enough for country people's foreign match money for a lifetime. After Sister-in-law Wang brought the matches over, he never retreated to the door frame, standing on the side of the table, holding one corner of the short table, and smiling at him: Yesterday, Mr. Meng talked about the things in the city so fun. I still want to hear more. Meng Guobao smiled: I will stay in the countryside for a few more days. When it is cool in the evening, I will talk to you. Wang Laoer put down the teacup, stretched, and yawned: I have to go and see the water in the field ditch. Meng Guobao stood up and smiled: That's right, I'm a little confused, how can I talk to you at noon and delay your work. Saying that, he stood up and walked towards the door. Sister-in-law Wang followed behind for two steps and smiled: It doesn't matter if you sit for a while. He went up the slope, and I didn't go. Meng Guobao had already left, and he couldn't go back, so he had to go home. He walked smoothly, walking along the embankment of the grass pond. The embankment was planted with catalpa trees, cypress branches, and the like. The shade of the trees covered the pond, and you could see large blue fish a foot long swimming in the water. So he stood under the tree, staring at the water in a daze. His heart was not on the fish, but on Sister-in-law Wang. He felt that country women were afraid of people and not afraid of people, not generous and generous, with a special kind of charm. Sister-in-law Wang had such good skin and such even bones and flesh. She really didn't look like a country woman, and she didn't look like the wife of a husband like Wang Laoer. Why did I have a good impression of her at first sight? I really don't understand. Oh! That's right. Doesn't she look a bit like Ms. Huanghou Shangsailan from Women's No. 1 High School? That's right, her dark eyes and long eyelashes are all similar. Just as he was thinking this, he heard a series of loud noises coming from the surface of the water. Looking up, on a washing stone across the pond, a woman was kneeling, holding a washing mallet in her hand, beating the clothes. It was Sister-in-law Wang, but she was wearing an old blue cloth jacket before, but now she was wearing a white coarse cloth jacket. When Meng Guobao looked over from this side, she stopped hammering the clothes and said loudly towards this side: Mr. Meng, you haven't left yet. Meng Guobao said: There are big fish in this pond. The more I look at them, the more I like them. As he spoke, he was afraid that the road was too far and it was a little difficult to hear clearly, so he walked back and stood under a weeping willow, holding the trunk of the tree, and said: Where's Laoer? Sister-in-law said: He went up the slope. As she spoke, she rolled up her sleeves, and her arms from below her elbows were exposed, so thick and strong, showing a kind of healthy beauty. She pressed the clothes with both hands, constantly rubbing them in the water or on the stone.

Film Special

Overseas Anecdotes

Hollywood Prophet Says About Jean Harlow's Future (Part 1) 234

—

After Jean Harlow continuously appeared with us in Shanghai-screened films such as "Platinum Blonde," "Goldie," and "Red-Headed Woman," the image of this blonde girl remains vividly in our minds. The death of Jean Harlow's husband, the famous director Paul Bern, by suicide, also caused a worldwide sensation, and this publication has previously reported on it. Therefore, the future of Jean Harlow is something many people want to know, and perhaps there is no need to first provide a detailed introduction to Jean's past.

The questions we want to know about Jean are: What is Jean doing now since her husband died? What will her future life be like? Can she permanently exist on the silver screen? And will she remarry, and will remarriage bring her happiness and recovery? Many people who care about Jean Harlow have already asked these questions repeatedly. But who can answer questions about a person's future? Even Jean herself cannot answer everything with the saying "Man can conquer nature." Now, three Hollywood prophets have answered these questions one by one. Why don't we adopt the attitude of "taking it with a grain of salt" and first publish it in our newspaper? If, after a year, what the Hollywood prophets have said has been confirmed one by one, wouldn't these few foreign "Zhuge Liangs" be more insightful than our blind fortune tellers?

These three prophets, one is good at observing celestial phenomena; one judges the future from tea leaves; and one perceives through a crystal ball. They have jointly torn open the curtain of the future, revealing the secrets of heaven. You may not believe their myths, but Jean Harlow herself has deeply converted to them.

Ms. Minnie Flyun, who was once famous on Broadway, is now the most prestigious prophet in Hollywood. A month before Paul married Jean, she discovered from tea leaves that a major figure in the film industry would soon encounter death, and that his death would be discovered within two months of marrying a blonde actress. After his death, the surroundings were shrouded in a mysterious atmosphere, and his death was most likely suicide. The above predictions have now all been proven true, because Paul married Jean for two months, and Paul has already shot himself in the head with a lead bullet and died. Minnie Flyun has many past miracles. Before Valentino died, she told Pola Negri that Valentino would soon die in the East. At that time, Valentino was not yet ill. Later, Valentino indeed fell ill and died in New York. She knew about the death of Ziegfeld, the great show business owner, before he died. Before the American giant ship Titanic struck a reef and sank in the Atlantic, she warned several important figures, who then changed to other ships and avoided the disaster. The following is Minnie's prediction for Jean Harlow:

"I see many things for Jean. I see that she will remarry within two years, to someone from the East. He is not in the film industry, but he has a slight connection to the film business. I believe she will be happy after remarrying, but many, many accidents will occur in the meantime.

"Jean will not leave the film industry because of this. The 'Red Dust' she is currently starring in will definitely be more popular than 'Hell's Angels' and 'Red-Headed Woman.' She will continue to play 'sex' roles. Between March and May of next year, there will be a scandalous case that will involve an Eastern businessman and a female writer in the film industry. This case will definitely be big, but it will not cause any harm to Jean.

"Although Paul Bern's death now feels extremely mysterious, it will definitely suddenly come to light soon, and Jean will not be involved in any unfavorable way." (To be continued)

Ms. Constance Bennett's most brilliant work since she started acting in movies is "What Price Hollywood?" The film will premiere tomorrow at the New Grand Theater.

Film Review

Review of "The Mayor's Nest" 235

— Ming

"The Mayor's Nest" is basically a comedy entirely sustained by "nonsense."

Sydney Howard plays a down-on-his-luck trumpet player who, because he is unemployed, spends his days looking for good fortune on the streets. Coincidentally, he meets an old lady who appreciates him very much. She campaigns for him to join the city council. Because he has experienced the taste of poverty, he advocates for the happiness of the common people. As a result, he gains popular support and is elected mayor. However, he still does not change his original intentions and enjoys himself with the people.

The foundation of such a script is based on "coincidence" and "fate." Rationally speaking, such lucky events simply do not exist in the world, especially for someone as foolish as the person Sydney plays. Strictly speaking, this film is nonsensical. However, in the excessive description, we can see that it still has some vitality. For example, it clearly states that "the gain of a fool" should not discourage those who are unsuccessful. At the same time, it also frankly describes that in British and American politics, the mayor does not necessarily have to be capable, but must be welcomed by the entire city to stand firm.

As for a completely comical and tasteless film, there is not much to comment on the director. Other technical aspects are also mediocre, but they can all be considered thoughtful. The contrasting scenes before and after are worth watching.

Sydney is truly an old-fashioned comedian. He doesn't use anything to assist him, but relies solely on his attitude, movements, and words to win the audience's laughter. His performance still follows the path he has taken in the past. I don't think that's outdated. I think it can give people a change of pace. The results this time are similar to "City Lights" and "Sea Breezes." Of course, it's not a regression, but there's no significant progress either. The two supporting actors, Claude Hulbert and Muriel Aked, are both very good, and people can't help but laugh when they see them. All the actors together have a humorous ability. The songs sung and the music played are also good stimulants.

One more thing to say is that it has a lot in common with "Gabriel Over the White House."

There are many laughs. If you are unhappy, then you can really go to Nanjing to laugh for an hour. Among British films, this film is rare!

Finally: I have to ask the authorities of the Nanjing Grand Theater, since this film is not long, then the supporting films are of course more important. But the three films shown yesterday, two of which were produced by "Pathe," were clearly made two weeks ago. (I don't remember if New Light has shown them, maybe Nanjing itself has shown them). I hope the first-class theaters will also pay more attention to these short films.

Edward G. Robinson's Anecdotes

— Cheng

"Edward G. Robinson, the protagonist of 'The Secret of the Blue Room,' which premiered at the Cathay, is Romanian and grew up in America. He has a superstition. He says that no matter what film he makes, his wife, Doris Lloyd, must join in, at least occupying a few scenes, regardless of the importance of the role, otherwise there will be no good results. So in 'Smart Money,' she played a waitress, and in 'Tiger Shark,' she played a guest at a wedding scene.

Also, cigars are his only hobby. People in Hollywood have never seen his mouth or hand without a cigar. When he is at home, he always smokes a pipe. In his house, there are all kinds of different sizes of pipes.

Hollywood Stories

The Struggles of Several Stars 236

— Shi Hongjun

Hollywood is the hometown of film talent. We must pay attention that the maturation of each star is not accidental. In her process, there must be her brave spirit, patient mind, and a history of struggling against her environment. The few stars mentioned here are all good examples for us.

Many people say that when the hot girl Clara Bow plays each role, her background often depicts her past and the resilient spirit of fighting life. Indeed, she has a very resilient spirit. She was born in Brooklyn. Her mother was ill. Clara's mother died when she was young, and her father was a waiter. She was very smart by nature. When she was not yet ten years old, she already understood the ways of the world. She knew that she was a poor orphan. In her teens, she grew up to be very beautiful, which gave her the opportunity to enter the film industry. When she first entered the film industry, she concealed her family situation, so no one laughed at her poverty.

Greta Garbo, who has recently gained fame, although she is only twenty-six years old, has gone through many servile lives in the past. She has worked as an assistant in a barber shop, as a model in a women's accessories store, and as a worthless actress. Then she drifted to Hollywood. When she first arrived in Hollywood, she was wearing a ragged skirt, short clothes, and thread socks. She did not understand the situation of life in the film industry at all. The arrogant and luxurious figures in Hollywood looked at her and were stunned and laughed. (To be continued)

Mary Pickford Injured While Filming 237

Hollywood telegram, 28th. American film star Mary Pickford was filming a new film today when a lamp suddenly fell and hit her forehead and eyebrows. Mary immediately fell and fainted. Her husband, Douglas Fairbanks, rushed her into her dressing room, and she gradually regained consciousness. The doctor said that the injury was not serious, but there was a broken skin on her forehead. It is feared that the filming work will be postponed until the scars have completely disappeared. (National Press)

Overseas News

Charlie Chaplin on His Son's Background 238

— Kang Bing

The lawsuit between Charlie Chaplin and his ex-wife Lita Grey over the issue of preventing his two children from entering the screen has now been declared over. Charlie has won the case. He is now preparing a reserve of 20,000 yuan to support his two children.

However, how does Charlie plan to arrange the future of his two children? Everyone is curiously inquiring. Does he hope to train them to become mechanics? Lawyers? Doctors, or politicians? Or even cooks? However, because Charlie's nature is unwilling to publicly disclose his own private affairs, this question is ultimately shelved.

Although he treasures his private affairs in this way, some opinions about his two children have been collected here. He believes that they should have a considerable education, which is more important than anything else. He is confident that they should have an opportunity to develop freely until they can decide their own profession. However, Charlie is very hasty about everything, so although he says so, it is not known whether the plan for these two children will change in the future. Maybe it will be like Douglas Fairbanks initially preventing Little Douglas Fairbanks from devoting himself to the screen, but now Little Douglas Fairbanks has become a star.

He is now thinking of writing a travelogue of his recent travels. He estimates it will be 50,000 words long. He said that the last part of this travelogue is more difficult to write than the beginning. However, he has recently finished the final chapter of more than 5,000 words.

Charlie's opinion on sound issues now seems to have changed slightly. He still believes that silent films occupy a quiet art, and he is very satisfied with the results of "City Lights." He has not yet decided whether his new film will be a silent film or a sound film. However, if it is a sound film, we can see a change in his style, or he may only direct and not act.

Star Biography

A Brief History of Dolores del Río 239

— Ji

丨The Mourner on the River丨

Dolores del Río, which translated into Spanish, means "The Mourner on the River." She was born in Mexico on August 3, 1905. She is a famous social flower in Mexican society. Before she entered the film industry, her original name was Dolores Asunsolo, a wealthy and noble Mexican lady. She was educated in Paris. Her intelligence is almost the same as her beauty. Her skin is like honey, smooth and light yellow. There is also a kind of jade-like purity of stone sculptures. This natural beauty is enough to make the many female stars in Hollywood pale in comparison. Her cloud-like hair and a pair of melancholy and affectionate eyes will fascinate anyone who sees them.

When Dolores was sixteen years old, she left school. At the same time, she married Mr. Jaime Del Río.

Although there are many frustrated people in Mexico, this couple had a happy ending. After their marriage, the two went to Europe on their honeymoon. During their leisure time, they concentrated on learning to dance. They once performed before the Spanish Emperor and Empress.

In 1925, the couple met a director in Mexico City named Edwin Carewe and went to Hollywood together, but she had never thought of movies before.

She first tried in the film "Joanna," starring Dorothy Mackaill, and became famous. Director Carewe praised her unparalleled appearance and performance art. He refused to let her go. She had to star in "High Steppers," "Resurrection," "Carmen," "The Loves of Carmen," and "Ramona" over and over again. Her sound film masterpiece is "Bad Girl." The lady is five feet five inches tall, weighs 110 pounds, with jade-colored black hair and beautiful brown eyes. She likes to sunbathe on the beach the most. She has a special interest in literature. During her leisure time, she always holds books and reads tirelessly. She can also speak five languages, making her the number one female star in Hollywood.

Film Monograph

"What Are You!" 241

— Chen Dabei

The twelfth expression practice is similar to the fourth. It is also a transition from fear to doubt.

The learner should first make a fearful expression in front of the mirror. Then, they seem to discover that the object of the previous fear does not exist. It is entirely a mistake of their own vision, but they dare not deny the existence of the object. Therefore, the eye sockets gradually shrink, and the mouth gradually closes tightly, making a "Huh? Wrong!" sound from the throat.

At this time, your head may shake naturally a couple of times. This is correct, because it is enough to prove that your emotion is indeed doubt.

The thirteenth style is connected to the twelfth style, so you should continue to practice.

Restore to the state of doubt just now, and then, like searching for the object that suddenly appeared just now and made you fearful, look at the shadow in the mirror with a detective-like gaze. Sure enough, the object has been found by you. It turns out that the person you usually look down on the most and are most unwilling to pay attention to is hiding there and joking with you.

Your gaze gradually turns into a state of jealousy. Stare straight at the shadow in the mirror. First, see if this expression can satisfy your own intentions. Then, use all your strength, after humming in the nasal cavity, shout loudly "What are you!"

Then, carefully observe how much power is added to your expression with the help of this pronunciation.
